CHAPTER 53: GARBAGE COLLECTION SERVICES
Section
   
53.01   Definitions
   
53.02   Responsibility of owner, occupant, or lessee of residence
   
53.03   Contracts
   
53.04   Number of collections; collection vehicles
   
53.05   Disposal of garbage
   
53.06   Container interference prohibited
   
53.07   Garbage in buildings
   
53.08   Collections by contractor only
   
53.09   Report of violations
   
53.10   Throwing or depositing of trash/refuse prohibited
   
53.11   Residences affected
   
53.12   Fee provisions
   
53.13   Fee amounts
   
53.14   Billing
   
53.15   Remedies
§ 53.01 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this chapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   CONTRACTOR. Any one or more persons, firms, or corporations having a
contractual relationship with the town for the collection and disposition of
garbage, or the employees or officials of the town collection and disposing of
garbage in the event a contact is not let for that work.
   GARBAGE.
      (1)   Any table matter that results in the preparation and use of meat,
fish, fowl, fruit, or vegetable matter; tin cans; glass cans; bottles; and
crockery which has been used as food or beverage holders;
      (2)   Any material resulting from ordinary household operations,
including such items as cans, glass, bottles, paper, magazines, newsprint,
boxes, rags, and small cartons; and
      (3)   Excluded from GARBAGE, and the related term REFUSE, are such items
as large boxes; furniture; appliances; springs; articles too large for packer-
type trucks; refrigerants; medications; tires; batteries; oil-based paints;
antifreeze; car fluids; fertilizer; aerosol cans; fire extinguishers;
radioactive materials; explosives; chemicals; hot ashes; televisions; phone
equipment; computer equipment; stereo equipment; all types of debris resulting
from repairing or remodeling any building such as dirt, wood, plaster, roofing,
pipes, cement blocks, broken concrete or stones; and, all lawn cuttings,
leaves, shrubbery, tree trimmings, dead animals, and animal excrement.
   OWNER. Any person, trust, firm, corporation, or association owning,
occupying, using, or inhabiting any premises for residence, business, or other
purposes within the corporate boundaries of the town.
   RESIDENCE. A single-family dwelling or a multi-family dwelling located
within the corporate boundaries of the town.
   TOWN. The Town of Fremont, Indiana.
(Ord. 2019-10, passed 12-17-2019; Am. Ord. 2022-01, passed 3-15-2022)
§ 53.02 RESPONSIBILITY OF OWNER, OCCUPANT, OR LESSEE OF RESIDENCE.
   The owner occupant, or lessee of any residence in the Town of Fremont shall
cause to be removed from said premises all garbage and refuse, and shall keep
said premises free and clear of any accumulation of garbage and refuse at all
times.
(Ord. 2014-08, passed - -2014; Am. Ord. 2022-01, passed 3-15-2022)
§ 53.03 CONTRACTS.
   The town may contract for the collection of garbage and refuse pursuant to
this chapter. The person or firm contracting to provide the service of
collecting and disposing of garbage and refuse shall give a good and sufficient
bond to the town in the sum equal to the yearly revenue under the contract for
satisfactory performance of duty or as otherwise required. The contractor shall
procure and keep in force such liability insurance as the Town Council may
require. The contractor shall be directly responsible to the Town Council,
whose duty shall be to see that the collection and disposal of garbage and
refuse is carried out according to the agreement between the contractor and the
town.
(1996 Code, § 6-56) (Ord. 2014-08, passed - - 2014; Am. Ord. 2022-01, passed 3-
15-2022) Penalty, see § 10.99
§ 53.04 NUMBER OF COLLECTIONS; COLLECTION VEHICLES.
   (A)   The town, or its duly authorized agent, shall collect all garbage and
refuse once each week from residences within the town, providing such garbage
and refuse is deposited in proper containers and placed on the street curb or
at the edge of an all-weather alley or in a location and at a time as
designated by the town, or its collecting agency, unless otherwise approved by
the Town Council. Said collection shall be scheduled between 6:00 a.m. local
time and 7:00 p.m. local time, on any single day of collection. All owners,
occupants, and lessees of any premises are thus required to have garbage and
refuse deposited in proper containers and placed at proper locations as
provided herein in a timely manner so that collection of said garbage and
refuse can occur between said times.
   (B)   Garbage and refuse must not exceed a total of 90 gallons per week per
approved container, and must be placed in a heavy duty roll-out cart of no more
than 90 gallon capacity, said cart to be made available by the town or its
agent. A residence may request the town or its agent, upon written request to
the town, to provide extra containers. All such containers shall be kept in a
sanitary condition. Garbage and refuse shall be carefully drained and wrapped
before depositing in approved containers, and other articles of unwieldy size
or shape will only be acceptable for collection if they are broken or cut down
to size suitable for handling and transporting. The Town Council shall have
authority to prescribe the maximum size and weight thereof from time to time
and have final authority for deciding if garbage is properly prepared. Any such
container shall be sufficiently closed to eliminate the spillage of garbage and
refuse.
(1996 Code, § 6-58) (Ord. 2014-08, passed - - 2014; Am. Ord. 2022-01, passed 3-
15-2022) Penalty, see § 10.99
§ 53.05 DISPOSAL OF GARBAGE.
   (A)   Garbage shall be removed from and disposed of beyond the corporate
limits of the town, at a location or locations as may be arranged for or
provided by the contractor, and in compliance with all applicable laws and
regulations.
   (B)   The place to which the garbage is removed or at which it is disposed
of even though outside the corporate limits of the town, shall not be closer
than 1,000 feet to the nearest occupied premises within the corporate limits.
(1996 Code, § 6-59) (Am. Ord. 2022-01, passed 3-15-2022) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 53.06 CONTAINER INTERFERENCE PROHIBITED.
   No persons, except authorized collectors of garbage, shall remove, damage,
meddle, or otherwise interfere with the garbage container of another, nor use
the same without permission of the owner thereof.
(Ord. 2014-08, passed - -2014; Am. Ord. 2022-01, passed 3-15-2022) Penalty, see
§
10.99
§ 53.07 GARBAGE IN BUILDINGS.
   No owner shall allow or cause any garbage or refuse to accumulate in the
basement or upon any floor of any house, building, or other structure, whether
inhabited or not, for more than 48 hours, unless said garbage or refuse is
deposited or contained in an approved container as herein provided.
(1996 Code, § 6-61) (Ord. 2014-08, passed - - 2014; Am. Ord. 2022-01, passed 3-
15-2022) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 53.08 COLLECTIONS BY CONTRACTOR ONLY.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to engage in the business of collecting
garbage in the Town of Fremont, Indiana, except a person, firm or corporation
engaging in a business under contract with the town pursuant to the provisions
of this section, or an official or employee of the town in the event a contract
for the work is not entered into; provided, however, that nothing herein
contained shall prevent or prohibit any person from collecting his or her own
garbage on his or her own premises and removing the same therefrom.
(1996 Code, § 6-62) (Am. Ord. 2022-01, passed 3-15-2022) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 53.09 REPORT OF VIOLATIONS.
   It shall be the duty of any collector of garbage to report any and all
violations of this chapter to either the Clerk-Treasurer, or any member of the
Town Council thereof in writing, and thereupon the town officials shall cause
the report to be investigated and to make complaint for violation of this
chapter in any and all proper cases.
(1996 Code, § 6-63) (Am. Ord. 2022-01, passed 3-15-2022) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 53.10 THROWING OR DEPOSITING OF TRASH/REFUSE PROHIBITED.
   It shall be unlawful for any person, firm or company, to throw, deposit or
suffer to throw or deposit or permit any rubbish, trash, garbage, refuse or any
other unwholesome material into or upon any public place or private place
except as provided by this chapter.
(1996 Code, § 6-65) (Am. Ord. 2022-01, passed 3-15-2022) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 53.11 RESIDENCES AFFECTED.
   (A)   Each residence is to receive garbage collection services to be
provided by the contractor awarded the garbage collection contract for the Town
of Fremont which collection services are to be subject to the terms and
conditions of the contract.
   (B)   Whenever there is a question as to whether this chapter applies, the
Clerk-Treasurer of the Town of Fremont is to make a determination which may be
appealed in writing by a party in interest to the Town Council.
(1996 Code, § 6-66) (Ord. 2014-08, passed - - 2014; Am. Ord. 2022-01, passed 3-
15-2022)
§ 53.12 FEE PROVISIONS.
   (A)   Findings. The Town Council finds that just and equitable garbage
collection services fees are those fees that provide sufficient revenue to pay
all expenses incident to the operation of administering a third-party garbage
collection service including, but not limited to, legal expenses, equipment,
transportation, town government garbage collection service, bookkeeping,
auditing, environmental and aesthetic maintenance, and customer relations. The
Town Council further finds that the fees established in this chapter are just
and equitable, as described herein.
   (B)   Service fee. The utility billing clerk shall assess a service fee for
garbage collection services in the amount provided in §
53.13 of this chapter ("Fee Amounts") to defray the cost charged to the town by
the contractor pursuant to a prior competitive bidding process.
   (C)   Administration fee. The utility billing clerk shall assess an
administration fee in the amount provided in §
53.13 of this chapter ("Fee Amounts") to help cover the administration costs
relating to garbage collection services.
   (D)   Late payment fee. The utility billing clerk shall assess a late
payment fee equal to 10% of the combined service fee and administration fee on
any utility bill that remains unpaid 30 days after having become due.
   (E)   Collection charges. The utility billing clerk shall assess collection
charges, including attorney and paralegal fees, to the utility bill, if
necessary, to ensure prompt payment.
   (F)   Costs. The utility billing clerk shall assess any garbage collection
service costs, such as for replacement containers or additional services, that
have been incurred by the town to the respective owner regarding whom the cost
is properly attributable.
   (G)   Taxes. The utility billing clerk shall assess any taxes for the above
fees and costs that are required to be imposed by law.
(Ord. 2022-01, passed 3-15-2022)
§ 53.13 FEE AMOUNTS.
   (A)   Service fee. The service fee for garbage collection services is
$13.44.
   (B)   Administration fee. The administration fee for garbage collection
services is $0.50.
(Ord. 2022-01, passed 3-15-2022)
§ 53.14 BILLING.
   (A)   Registration. Each residence owner shall ensure that at least one
owner of the residence has registered for garbage collection services with the
utility billing clerk. The owner(s) of record must be the same owner(s) of
record for sewer works service.
   (B)   Hold harmless. By registering for garbage collection services, each
residence owner thereby holds the town harmless from any loss, including all
penalties, fines, fees, attorney's fees, interest, and court costs, or other
loss if any, for suspension of garbage collection services pursuant to a
violation of this chapter.
   (C)   Billing. The utility billing clerk shall send out a monthly bill for
garbage collection services to each residence; provided, however, that in the
case of a covered residence that is not connected to municipal water, the
utility billing clerk may opt to send the bill on a quarterly basis.
   (D)   Duty to pay. Each residence owner shall timely pay, or ensure that
another person has timely paid, the respective bill for garbage collection
services. Each owner is jointly and severally liable for its payment.
   (E)   Private contracts. Where this chapter conflicts with the terms of a
contract entered into by the Town Council, the terms of the contract control
with respect to the parties, any residence that is the subject of the contract,
and, as justice may require, to any other person at the residence. If an act
would be a violation under this chapter but is specifically permitted in a
contract entered into with the Town Council, the act is instead not a
violation.
(Ord. 2022-01, passed 3-15-2022)
§ 53.15 REMEDIES.
   (A)   Service suspension. In addition to any late payment fees and
collection costs assessed by the town, if the Town Manager (or if generally
unavailable, the Clerk-Treasurer) has reasonable suspicion to believe that a
material violation of this chapter has occurred, he or she may authorize and/or
direct the contractor to confiscate the respective residence container and/or
to not collect the garbage at that residence until the Town Manager receives
satisfactory assurances that the circumstances leading to the violation have
been abated.
   (B)   Extraneous claims barred. No owner shall have recourse against the
town, the Town Council, the Town Manager, the Clerk-Treasurer, the contractor,
or their respective agents to the extent the contractor has not collected
garbage from a residence because the container was not timely placed curbside,
because the owner violated this chapter or other applicable law or rules, or
because the Town Manager or Clerk-Treasurer directed the contractor not to
collect the garbage from the unit.
   (C)   Continuing liability. If the contractor does not collect the garbage
of an owner pursuant to a violation of this chapter, the owner remains liable
for any public nuisance created by the uncollected garbage and remains liable
for payment of the utility bill.
(Ord. 2022-01, passed 3-15-2022)
TITLE VII: TRAFFIC CODE
   Chapter

CHAPTER 70: GENERAL PROVISIONS
Section
   
70.01   Off-street vehicle regulations
   
70.02   Jake-braking prohibited
   
70.03   Passenger restraint in motor vehicles
   
70.99   Penalty
§ 70.01 OFF-STREET VEHICLE REGULATIONS.
   (A)   All use and operation of off-road vehicles and snowmobiles at Fremont
Recreational Park is prohibited.
   (B)   For the purpose of this section, the following definition shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
      OFF-ROAD VEHICLES. Any motor driven vehicle capable of cross country
travel, without benefit of a road or trail, on or immediately over land, water,
snow, ice, marsh, swampland or other natural terrain. They include, but are not
limited to, a multi-wheel drive or low pressure tire vehicle, amphibious
machine, ground effect air cushion vehicle or other means of transportation
deriving motor power from a source other than muscle or wind.
(1996 Code, § 8-45)
§ 70.02 JAKE-BRAKING PROHIBITED.
   When signs are erected giving notice thereof it shall be illegal for the
drivers of semi-tractors to use the procedure known as Jake-braking within the
town limits of Fremont.
(1996 Code, § 8-48)
§ 70.03 PASSENGER RESTRAINT IN MOTOR VEHICLES.
   (A)   Definitions.  For purposes of this section the following words and
phrases shall have the following meanings ascribed them respectively:
      CHILD PASSENGER RESTRAINT SYSTEM.  A device that is manufactured for the
purposes of protecting children from injury during a motor vehicle accident and
meets the standards prescribed in I.C. 9-13-2-23 and 49 CFR 571.213.
      PASSENGER MOTOR VEHICLE. For the purposes of this chapter, shall mean a
motor vehicle designed for carrying passengers and does not include a
motorcycle, bus, or school bus, tractor, or recreational vehicle.
   (B)   Front seat passenger. All occupants of a passenger motor vehicle that
is equipped with a safety belt meeting the standards stated in the Federal
Motor Vehicle Safety Standard 208 (49 CFR 571.208) shall have a safety belt
properly fastened about the occupant's body at all times when the vehicle is in
forward motion.
   (C)   Child restraint requirements.
      (1)   A person who operates a motor vehicle in which there is a child
less than 4 years of age shall have said child restrained by a child passenger
restraint system, however, if it is reasonably determined that the child will
not fit in a child restraint system then said child shall be properly fastened
and restrained by a safety belt.
      (2)   A person who operates a passenger motor vehicle that is equipped
with a safety belt meeting the requirements stated in the Federal Motor Vehicle
Safety Standard Number 208 (49 CFR 571.208) shall have every child at least 4
years of age but less than 12 years of age properly fastened and restrained by
a child passenger restraint system or a safety belt.
   (D)   Vehicle stop. A vehicle may be stopped by the Police Department to
determine compliance with this section. However, a vehicle, the contents of the
vehicle, the driver of the vehicle, or a passenger in a vehicle may not be
inspected, searched, or detained solely because of a violation of this section.
(Ord. 2008-05, passed 5-12-2008)
§ 70.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no
specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99.
   (B)   Any person violating any provision of §
70.01 shall be subject to the fine of $10 to $100 for each violation thereof.
(1996 Code, § 8-45)
   (C)   Any person who shall violate any of the provisions of §
70.02 shall be fined a sum not to exceed $100.
(1996 Code, § 8-48)
   (D)   Each violation of §
70.03 shall, in addition to any other penalty, subject the operator thereof
said vehicle to a fine of not less than $25 nor more than $1,000 for each
violation by each occupant in said vehicle.
(Ord. 2008-05, passed 5-12-2008)
CHAPTER 71: TRAFFIC REGULATIONS
Section
   
71.01   Definitions
   
71.02   Specific regulations
   
71.03   Three-way stop created
   
71.04   General speed limit
   
71.05   Roller skates and other recreation
   
71.06   Golf carts
 
   
71.99   Penalty
§ 71.01 DEFINITIONS.
   The definitions of state law regulating traffic on highways, I.C. 9-13-2-
1 et seq. shall govern all provisions of this chapter.
(1996 Code, § 8-1)
§ 71.02 SPECIFIC REGULATIONS.
   (A)   All drivers must keep to the right side of 2-way streets.
   (B)   It is unlawful for vehicles, either horse or motor driven to enter the
pavement before coming to a complete stop.
   (C)   It is unlawful for vehicles to enter or turn on the public square of
the town before coming to a complete stop.
   (D)   It is unlawful for vehicles to make a complete turn on the public
square.
   (E)   It shall be the duty of the Town Marshal to enforce this section.
(1996 Code, § 8-2) Penalty, see §
71.99
§ 71.03 THREE-WAY STOP CREATED.
   (A)   Upon an engineering and traffic investigation, the Town Council has
determined that certain stop signs shall be erected at specific entrances.
   (B)   The town employees directed by the Council shall erect stop signs as
indicated: The intersection of Jefferson Street and North Street in the Town of
Fremont is established as a 3-way stop.
   (C)   The stop signs erected shall conform to the manual on Uniform Traffic
Control Devices for roads and streets as provided under I.C. 9-21-2 et seq.,
I.C. 9-21-3 et seq., and I.C. 9-21-4 et seq.
   (D)   Every driver of a vehicle shall stop in obedience to any stop sign
before entering intersections, except when directed to proceed by a police
officer.
   (E)   Penalties for violation of this section shall be as set forth in I.C.
9-21-4-19 and that the provisions thereof are enacted by reference as if fully
set out herein.
(1996 Code, § 8-6)
§ 71.04 GENERAL SPEED LIMIT.
   Speed shall be regulated on all streets in the Town of Fremont, Indiana, at
30 mph unless otherwise posted.
(1996 Code, § 8-20) Penalty, see §
71.99
§ 71.05 ROLLER SKATES AND OTHER RECREATION.
   (A)   For the purpose of this section, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
      DOWNTOWN CENTRAL BUSINESS DISTRICT. The area encompassing the real
property located adjacent to Toledo Street from the centerline of that certain
roadway commonly known as Coffin Street, thence east to the centerline of that
certain roadway commonly known as Mill Street in the Town of Fremont, Indiana.
      RECKLESS or HAZARDOUS OPERATION.
         (a)   The operation of a skateboard or other wheeling or sliding
device in a manner so that the wheels of a wheeling device leave the ground or
that the skateboard or sliding device is separated from the ground at the same
time (i.e. airborne).
         (b)   It is further defined to mean the use of disability ramps,
steps, walls, retention walls, doors, handrails, planters, curb or gutter
edges, barriers and barricades, benches, picnic tables, sculptures, stages,
platforms, playground equipment or other device or structure which is not
intended for pedestrian or vehicular traffic, jumping or stepping on or off the
devices or structures using wheeled equipment, or in a manner that is likely to
cause damage to property or to cause personal injury or failing to yield the
right of way to or otherwise interfere with pedestrian traffic.
      SKATEBOARD. A foot board mounted upon 4 or more wheels and usually
propelled by the user who sometimes stands, sits, kneels or lies upon the
device while it is in motion.
      WHEELING OR SLIDING DEVICES. Include, but are not limited to,
skateboards, roller skates, in-line skates or any other device containing
wheels which can be ridden on or otherwise utilized by an individual or
individuals in order to move about other than walking, with the exception of
human powered bicycles.
   (B)   The operation of a skateboard or other wheeling or sliding device
shall be prohibited as follows:
      (1)   In the Downtown Central Business District, the operation of
skateboards or other wheeling or sliding devices shall be prohibited at all
times;
      (2)   No person shall operate a skateboard or other wheeling or sliding
device in a reckless or hazardous manner within the corporate boundaries of the
Town of Fremont, except as specifically permitted, and only in a manner
specifically permitted, in designated town skate park areas;
      (3)   (a)   No person shall operate a skateboard or other wheeling or
sliding device upon any property where a sign or signs are posted by property
owners prohibiting that operation.
         (b)   This provision shall be interpreted to mean that if a sign is
posted prohibiting skateboarding it shall be deemed to apply to the prohibition
of all skateboard or other wheeling or sliding devices; and
      (4)   Notwithstanding the definition of skateboard or other wheeling or
sliding device, nothing in this section shall prohibit the use of a wheelchair,
a stroller or similar devices, for the purpose of helping an elderly, disabled
individual, infant or other individual needing assistance in moving from place
to place.
(Ord. 2004-18, passed 8-9-2004) Penalty, see §
71.99
§ 71.06 GOLF CARTS.
   (A)   The following vehicles, which this section allows for, shall be
defined as follows:
      GOLF CART. As used in this section, is defined as any four-wheeled motor
vehicle originally  and specially designed and intended to transport one or
more individuals and golf clubs for the purpose of playing the game of golf on
a golf course.
      UTILITY TASK VEHICLE (UTV). As used in this section, is defined as any
off-road vehicle that: (a) has a width greater than 51 inches but not exceeding
65 inches; (b) a dry weight of at least 1,201 pounds, but not exceeding 2,000
pounds; (c) is designed for travel on at least four non-highway or off-highway
tires; (d) is designed for recreational use by one or more individuals; and (e)
is designed to be steered, driven or controlled with a steering wheel. As used
in the previous sentence, the term "steering wheel" shall not include
handlebars. The definition for UTV shall not be construed to include all-
terrain vehicles ("ATV") as currently defined in I.C. 14-8-2-5.7. No individual
shall use, operate, drive, or park an ATV on the streets, alleys, and
properties under the jurisdiction of the town.
   (B)   A person may operate, drive or park ("operate") a golf cart or UTV on
the streets, alleys, and properties under the jurisdiction of the town subject
to the rules and restrictions set forth herein.
   (C)   Operators of golf carts or UTVs must have a valid driver's license and
shall obey all state, federal, and local laws, regulations, and ordinances
governing passenger motor vehicles, including but not limited to laws,
regulations, and ordinances pertaining to licensing of operators and traffic
regulations.
   (D)   Golf carts or UTVs operated during darkness from dusk to dawn, or
during inclement weather, when headlamps are necessary for motor vehicles, must
be equipped with and use headlights, taillights with brake lights, and turn
signals visible from a distance of not less than 500 feet.
   (E)   Golf carts or UTVs shall be driven as close to the right edge of the
street or alley as possible.
   (F)   No person shall operate a golf cart or UTV on a sidewalk.
   (G)   No person shall operate or permit the operation of a golf cart or UTV
without proof of financial responsibility, as further set forth in division (O)
herein, which must be made available upon request by town or state officials.
   (H)   No person shall operate a golf cart or UTV unless any and all
passengers of said golf cart or UTVs are seated in a seat attached to the golf
cart or UTV as manufactured. In no event shall a person operate a golf cart or
UTV unless the operator and all passengers are completely within the perimeter
of the golf cart or UTV.
   (I)   Any golf cart or UTV shall be equipped with a rear view mirror and
factory seating. The occupancy of the golf cart or UTV shall not exceed that
contemplated by the factory seating. No person under the age of two years shall
be allowed to ride on a golf cart or UTV and all persons under the age of ten
years must only ride in the front seat of the golf cart or UTV. The driver and
all passengers in the golf cart or UTV must be seated while it is in motion.
   (J)   No person shall operate a golf cart or UTV unless it is equipped with
and displays a triangular slow moving vehicle emblem or a red, or amber,
flashing lamp that is entirely visible from the rear of the golf cart or UTV at
all times. In addition, no person shall operate a golf cart or UTV unless it is
equipped with and displays an orange flag or pennant attached to a pole so that
the flag or pennant is at least seven feet above the surface of the street.
   (K)   No person shall operate a golf cart or UTV so that it impedes or
blocks the normal flow of traffic.
   (L)   The Town Council may exempt any use of a golf cart or UTV by a town
employee or official from the provisions of this section when it is determined
that the same is necessary to properly perform the functions of the town.
   (M)   Any person, firm, or corporation who violates, or permits a violation
of any provisions of this section shall pay a fine not to exceed $200. Money
collected for fines shall be deposited in the general fund. Any person, firm,
or corporation who violates, or permits a violation of any provisions of this
section commits a Class C infraction.
   (N)   No person shall operate a golf cart or UTV without valid registration
with the town. The Town Clerk-Treasurer shall make forms available for the
registration of golf carts or UTV and shall collect all fees for registration.
The annual registration fee shall be $40, except that any registration which
requires the issuance of plates (typically only the initial registration) shall
instead cost $55. Each registration shall last from January 1 to December 31 of
each year but may not be prorated for portions of the year already lapsed.
   (O)   Additional registration requirements. The following steps are also
required for the registration of a golf cart or UTV with the Clerk-Treasurer:
      (1)   Prior to registration, the golf cart or UTV must have been
inspected by the Town Marshal or his or her deputy to ensure it complies with
the equipment requirements of this section.
      (2)   At the time of registration, the owner of the golf cart or UTV
shall present proof of insurance for the golf cart or UTV, which must include
coverage for property damage and personal liability coverage for injury or
damage to property of others and for personal injury to other persons with a
minimum combined single limit of $100,000. Such insurance must be maintained on
the golf cart or UTV for as long as it is operated on streets, alleys, and
properties under the jurisdiction of the Town of Fremont.
(Ord. 2015-03, passed 7-21-2015; Am. Ord. 2017- 03, passed 7-18-2017)
§ 71.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no
specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99.
   (B)   Any person or persons violating any of the provisions of §
71.02, upon conviction thereof, shall be fined for the first offense the sum of
$5, second offense $20 and third offense $50. Each violation constituting a
separate offense.
(1996 Code, § 8-2)
   (C)   (1)   Any person who shall violate any of the provisions of §
71.04 shall be fined in a sum not to exceed $300.
(1996 Code, § 8-20)
      (2)   Anyone violating any provisions of the maximum speed limits
established by §
71.04 shall be guilty of a Class C Infraction.
(1996 Code, § 8-26)
   (D)   (1)   Any individual operating a skateboard or other wheeling or
sliding device in violation of any of the provisions contained in §
71.05 shall be subject to a fine of $50 per violation.
      (2)   In addition to the fine, any person found in violation of any
provision of §
71.05 may have the skateboard or other wheeling or sliding device confiscated
immediately by the Fremont Police Department or by any officer of the Fremont
Police Department acting in his or her official capacity in order to abate the
nuisance.
      (3)   The skateboard or wheeling or sliding device confiscated shall be
held for a maximum of 90 days after which it may be sold or destroyed.
      (4)   The individual who owns any confiscated skateboard or wheeling or
sliding device shall have the right to repossess the skateboard or wheeling or
sliding device upon proof of payment of any fine and other costs for which the
individual is responsible as a result of having violated the provisions set
forth in §
71.05.
      (5)   Any individual violator of this section who is under the age of 18
years of age must disclose to the police officer or other enforcing authority
the names, addresses and phone numbers of their parents or legal guardian.
(Ord. 2004-18, passed 8-9-2004)
CHAPTER 72: PARKING REGULATIONS
Section
   
72.01   Restricted parking of house trailers
   
72.02   Stopping, standing or parking regulations
   
72.03   Adjacent to roadways during snow accumulation
   
72.99   Penalty
§ 72.01 RESTRICTED PARKING OF HOUSE TRAILERS.
   (A)   No house trailer shall be parked within the Fire Zone of the town,
except those trailers that are held for resale by an authorized dealer may be
parked on a lot for display purposes only.
   (B)   All trailers must remain unoccupied.
(1996 Code, § 8-15) Penalty, see §
72.99
§ 72.02 STOPPING, STANDING OR PARKING REGULATIONS.
   No person shall stop, stand or park a vehicle, except when necessary to
avoid conflict with other traffic or the directions of a police officer or
traffic control device in any of the following places:
   (A)   Upon a road within the town which results in obstructing traffic;
   (B)   On a sidewalk;
   (C)   In front of a public or private driveway;
   (D)   Within an intersection;
   (E)   Within 15 feet of a fire hydrant;
   (F)   On a crosswalk;
   (G)   Within 20 feet of a crosswalk at an intersection;
   (H)   Within 20 feet of a driveway entrance to any fire station and on the
side of a street opposite the entrance to any fire station within 75 feet of
the entrance when properly posted;
   (I)   On the roadway side of any vehicle stopped or parked at the edge or
curb of a street; or
   (J)   At any place where official signs prohibit stopping.
(1996 Code, § 8-17) Penalty, see §
72.99
§ 72.03 ADJACENT TO ROADWAYS DURING SNOW ACCUMULATION.
   (A)   All vehicles parked upon any public roadway located within the
jurisdiction of the Town of Fremont, Indiana, shall be moved a minimum of 1
time in every 24-hour period during those periods of snow accumulation in
excess of 2 inches within any 24-hour period.
   (B)   The Fremont Police Department is hereby authorized to retain the
services of a properly licensed and qualified vehicle towing operator to remove
any vehicle found in violation of this section, at the sole cost and expense of
the owner of any like vehicle.
(Ord. 2004-01, passed 2-9-2004) Penalty, see §
72.99
§ 72.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no
specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99.
   (B)   Violation of §
72.02 shall be subject to a minium fine of $2 for each offense, payable to the
Clerk-Treasurer.
(1996 Code, § 8-17)
   (C)   Any person violating any of the provisions of §
72.03 shall be subject to a fine of not less than $20 nor more than $75 for
each violation thereof. The provisions of this section shall be enforced by the
Fremont Police Department.
(Ord. 2004-01, passed 2-9-2004)
CHAPTER 73: TRUCK ROUTE REGULATIONS
Section
   
73.01   Semi-trailers restricted
   
73.02   Commercial delivery restrictions
   
73.03   Load restrictions
   
73.04   Truck routes established
   
73.05   Definitions
   
73.06   Exceptions
   
73.07   Semi-trailer and tractor parking restrictions
   
73.08   Alternative temporary truck routes
   
73.99   Penalty
§ 73.01 SEMI-TRAILERS RESTRICTED.
   No semi-trailer is to be driven or hauled upon any public street or
thoroughfare in the Town of Fremont except as allowed herein.
(1996 Code, § 8-31)
§ 73.02 COMMERCIAL DELIVERY RESTRICTIONS.
   Any semi-trailer traveling or being hauled to make a commercial delivery at
any site in the Town of Fremont not accessible via truck routes as established
herein and meeting weight restrictions applicable to State Road 120 and County
Road 827 may travel by the shortest route available to the delivery site for
the purpose of making the delivery and returning therefrom without unreasonable
delay shall be permitted.
(1996 Code, § 8-32)
§ 73.03 LOAD RESTRICTIONS
   (A)   One loaded semi-trailer may be driven or hauled to the residence of an
operator provided:
      (1)   That the loaded weight of the trailer does not exceed 9,000 pounds;
and
      (2)   That the operator lived at the residence prior to the adoption of
this section regularly drove or hauled semi-trailers to the residence prior to
the adoption of this section, and the operator certifies by the affidavit that
the facts required by this division exists and files the same with the Town
Council within 30 days of the first publication of this section, the affidavit
is to state the legal description of the real estate upon which the residence
is located and is to be prepared in recordable form and accompanied with funds
to cover the cost of recording the same with the Steuben County Recorder.
   (B)   The Clerk-Treasurer is to cause any affidavits filed pursuant to this
division to be filed with the Steuben County Recorder.
(1996 Code, § 8-33)
§ 73.04 TRUCK ROUTES ESTABLISHED.
   The following areas are to be declared truck routes and loaded semi-trailers
meeting the weight restrictions applicable to State Road 120 are permitted
thereon:
   (A)   State Road 827;
   (B)   State Road 120;
   (C)   West Street;
   (D)   Peachey Road;
   (E)   Depot Street;
   (F)   Clear Lake/Ray Road;
   (G)   Water Street;
   (H)   Coffin Street (between Water and Pearl);
   (I)   County Road 375 East (S. Depot Street);
   (J)   Coldwater Street;
   (K)   Hardy Street (between Tillotson Street and the eastern terminus of
Hardy Street); and
   (L)   N. Wayne Street.
(1996 Code, § 8-34) (Ord. 2004-12, passed 5-10-2004)
§ 73.05 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this chapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   COMMERCIAL DELIVERY. A delivery to any commercial or industrial facility,
and any moving van moving residential personal furniture and property, or any
delivery of consumer goods to a residence by any person or entity other than
the owner or resident thereof, or any dump truck or delivery truck delivering
construction materials or fill to a construction site where the facility or
site is not conveniently accessible from a truck route, or any garbage or
refuse truck collecting garbage or refuse from a set-out site within the town,
or any trailer or tractor brought to a garage for repair.
   SEMI-TRAILER. Any semi-trailer or any dumptruck and does not require that
the trailer be full of cargo.
(1996 Code, § 8-35)
§ 73.06 EXCEPTIONS.
   The restrictions set forth herein shall not apply to any snow plow, fire
truck, municipally or governmentally owned vehicle, or to any vehicle owned by
any school district, or any emergency vehicle.
(1996 Code, § 8-36)
§ 73.07 SEMI-TRAILER AND TRACTOR PARKING RESTRICTIONS.
   (A)   No semi-trailer is to be parked on any paved portion of any street or
highway or any paved portion of any street or highway right-of-way within the
municipality for more than 2 hours nor is any semi-trailer to be parked in any
manner so as to interfere with street cleaning, repairs or snow removal.
   (B)   Any semi-trailer parked on any unpaved portion of a street right-of-
way is parked at owner’s risk including risk of being plowed in with snow
during snow removal by municipality.
   (C)   One semi-tractor may be parked at the residence of the operator
provided that the tractor is not left running for more than 45 minutes at any 1
time or for more than 45 minutes during any 8-hour period.
(1996 Code, § 8-37)
§ 73.08 ALTERNATIVE TEMPORARY TRUCK ROUTES.
   (A)   The Town Marshal may by order designate alternative temporary truck
routes for parades, street fairs and other special events as the Marshal deems
appropriate.
   (B)   Tractors and trailers escorted to the court by law enforcement
officers to attend initial town hearings or tractors and trailers brought to
the court in compliance with a court order are permitted to leave the truck
routes in order to travel to and from the site of the court by the most direct
route.
(1996 Code, § 8-38)
§ 73.99 PENALTY.
   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no specific
penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99.

CHAPTER 90: PARKS AND RECREATION
Section
   
90.01   Authority to operate
   
90.02   Park and recreation sites within Fremont
   
90.03   Rules and regulations for the operation of public parks
   
Appendix A: Park and recreation sites
§ 90.01 AUTHORITY TO OPERATE.
   (A)   Under the provisions of Acts 1981, P.L. 309, SEC 110, (I.C. 36-10-3-3)
there is hereby established a Department of Parks and Recreation, composed of
the Parks and Recreation Board (hereafter referred to as Board,) a
superintendent and other personnel as the Board may determine.
   (B)   (1)   The Board shall consist of 4 members to be appointed by the Town
Council President.
      (2)   The members shall be appointed on the basis of their interest in
and knowledge of parks and recreation, but no more than 2 members may be
affiliated with the same political party.
   (C)   In addition the Town Council may provide for 1 or 2 ex-officio
members, those being:
      (1)   A member of the governing body of the school corporation selected
by that body;
      (2)   A member of the governing body of the library district selected by
that body; or
      (3)   Both (1) and (2).
   (D)   Ex-officio members have all the rights of regular members, including
the right to vote. A vacancy in an ex-officio position shall be filled by the
appointing authority.
   (E)   Initial appointments to the Board are as follows: 1 member for a term
of 1 year; 1 member for a term of 2 years; 1 member for a term of 3 years; 1
member for a term of 4 years.
   (F)   (1)   The Town Council President shall make the initial appointments
within 90 days of the adoption of this section.
      (2)   Thereafter, as a term expires, each new appointment is for a 4-year
term.
      (3)   All terms expire on the first Monday in January, but a member
continues in office until his or her successor is appointed.
      (4)   If an appointment for any new term is not made by the first Monday
in April, the incumbent shall serve another term.
      (5)   If a vacancy on the Board occurs, the Town Council President shall
appoint a person to serve for the remainder of the unexpired term.
   (G)   (1)   All meetings of the Board are open to the public. The Board
shall fix the time and place of the regular meetings, but shall meet at least
quarterly.
      (2)   At its first regular meeting each year the Board shall elect a
President and a Vice President.
      (3)   The Vice President may act as president during the absence or
disability of the President. The Board may select a Secretary either from
within or outside its membership.
   (H)   The Board shall have the general power to perform all acts necessary
to acquire and develop sites and facilities and to conduct programs as are
generally understood to be park and recreation functions. In addition to all
other powers necessary to achieve the general objectives of the Board, the
Board shall have, for park and recreation purposes, all the powers and duties
listed in 110 Acts 1981, P.L. 309, amended by Acts 1981. P.L. 320, SEC. 6; P.L.
228-1986, § 1.
(I.C. 36-10-3-10 and 36-10-3-11) (1996 Code, § 5-1)
§ 90.02 PARK AND RECREATION SITES WITHIN FREMONT.
   The map in Appendix A depicts the existing and future park and recreation
sites.
(1996 Code, § 5-2)
§ 90.03 RULES AND REGULATIONS FOR THE OPERATION OF PUBLIC PARKS.
   (A)   Fremont public parks shall be open to the public from 5:00 a.m. to 11:
00 p.m. each day. Playground areas, including the skate park, may be used from
8:00 a.m. to 10:00 p.m. each day, weather permitting.
   (B)   Motorized vehicles shall be parked in designated parking areas only,
with the exception of designated parking areas, all motorized vehicles are
prohibited on park grounds.
   (C)   Pets are not allowed in public parks unless the pet is on a leash and/
or under the control of the handler. The handler must comply with all town
ordinances pertaining to animals, including noise, running at large, impounding
of and sanitation procedures. (See
Chapter 92: Animals of the Fremont Code of Ordinances.)
   (D)   Open fires, except in fireplaces, charcoal pits and grills, shall not
be permitted in any public park and shall not be allowed inside or under any
pavilion or roofed structure.
   (E)   Swimming and wading is prohibited in any body of water located on
public park property.
   (F)   Camping is not allowed in any public park without the prior approval
of the Fremont Town Council.
   (G)   Alcohol and controlled drugs, unless prescribed by a physician, are
prohibited on public park property.
   (H)   Park facilities, pavilions, fields and the like, may be reserved at
the Fremont Town Hall, 205 N. Tolford Street, on a first come first serve
basis, beginning on the first working day after January 1 of each year, or at
any time thereafter so long as the facility requested is available. There are
fees involved for reserving the park pavilion, costs are subject to change and
information on costs and deposits can be obtained at the Clerk-Treasurer’s
office, Town Hall, 260-495-7805.
   (I)   All law enforcement officers and any town employees are authorized to
enforce public park rules and regulations. Failure to follow rules and
regulations will result in the expulsion from park property and/or fines and
arrest it applicable town ordinances are violated or individuals resist
expulsion.
   (J)   The Town Council may issue exceptions to any of the above rules for
special events sponsored by the town or for other special events approved by
the Council prior to the event.
(Res. 2009-03, passed 4-21-2009) Penalty, see §
10.99
Cross-Reference:
   Park pavilion rentals, garage sales and farmers market vendor permit fees,
see §
111.06

GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 91.001 AUTHORITY TO REGULATE.
   The town may regulate the conduct, or use or possession of property which
might endanger the public health, safety or welfare of its citizens.
(1996 Code, § 6-1)
§ 91.002 PRESERVATION OF PUBLIC PEACE AND ORDER.
   The town may establish, maintain and operate a police and law enforcement
system to preserve public peace and order and may provide facilities and
equipment for that system.
(1996 Code, § 6-2)
§ 91.003 AUTHORITY TO REGULATE AIR AND SOUND.
   The town may regulate the introduction of any substance or odor into the
air, or any generation of sound.
(1996 Code, § 6-3)
§ 91.004 AUTHORITY TO REGULATE PUBLIC GATHERINGS.
   The town may regulate public gatherings, such as shows, demonstrations,
fairs, conventions, sporting events and exhibitions.
(1996 Code, § 6-4)
§ 91.005 SMOKING; CIGARS, PIPES, CIGARETTES AND WEED PLANTS.
   (A)   Purpose. The purpose of this section is to protect the public health
and welfare by prohibiting smoking on town-owned vehicles and buildings,
including, but not limited to fire stations, police stations, Fremont utility
buildings, Street Department buildings, park restrooms and assembly halls; and
to guarantee the right of nonsmokers to breathe smoke-free air, and to
recognize that the need to breathe smoke-free air shall have priority over the
desire to smoke.
   (B)   Definitions. For the purpose of this section, the following
definitions shall apply unless the context clearly indicates or requires a
different meaning.
      EMPLOYEE. A person who is employed by the Town of Fremont and receives
direct monetary wages or profit.
      EMPLOYER. The Town of Fremont.
      ENCLOSED AREA. All space between a floor and ceiling that is enclosed on
all sides by solid walls or windows (exclusive of doorways), which extend from
the floor to the ceiling.
      SMOKING. Burning and carrying, inhaling or exhaling, of any lighted
cigar, cigarette, pipe, containing any weed or plant.
      TOWN OF FREMONT PROPERTY. All properties owned by The Town of Fremont,
including but not limited to the Town Hall, fire stations, fire apparatus,
police station, police vehicles, Fremont municipal utility buildings, Fremont
municipal utility vehicles, Street Department buildings, Street Department
vehicles, park restrooms and assembly halls.
   (C)   Posting of signs.
      (1)   “No Smoking” signs and/or the international “No Smoking” symbol
(consisting of a pictorial representation of a burning cigarette enclosed in a
red circle with a red bar across it) shall be clearly and conspicuously posted
at all buildings, including the Town Hall, fire stations, police stations,
Fremont municipal utility buildings and Street Department buildings owned by
the Town of Fremont.
      (2)   All Town of Fremont property shall have posted at every entrance to
an enclosed area a conspicuous sign clearly stating/indicating that smoking is
prohibited.
      (3)   All ashtrays and other smoking paraphernalia shall be removed from
Town of Fremont property (except for the vehicles owned or used by the Town of
Fremont).
   (D)   Smoking on Fremont property prohibited.
Smoking is prohibited within all enclosed areas on Town of Fremont property.
   (E)   Enforcement.
      (1)   This section shall be enforced by the Town Manager, an authorized
designee, any law enforcement officer or department head.
      (2)   Notice of the provisions of this section shall be given to all
applicants who seek employment with the Town of Fremont.
      (3)   Notwithstanding any other provision of this section, an employee or
private citizen may bring action to enforce this section.
      (4)   In addition to the remedies provided by the provisions of this
section, the Manager or any person aggrieved by the failure of the authorized
designee, or department head or other person in control of town owned property
to comply with the provisions of this section may apply for injunctive relief
to enforce those provisions in any court of competent jurisdiction.
(Ord. 2005-15, passed 7-19-2005) Penalty, see §
91.999
BURNING AND FIRE REGULATIONS
§ 91.015 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this chapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   BURNING CONTAINER. A metal or masonry inclosure with no more than 3/4-inch
openings at the top.
   RUBBISH. Matter such as ashes, can, metal wear, broken glass, crockery,
sweepings, boxes, wood, glass, weeds, paper or litter of any kind.
(1996 Code, § 6-21)
Cross-reference:
   Fireworks, see
Ch. 96
§ 91.016 REQUIREMENTS.
   (A)   No person, firm or corporation within the corporation limits of the
Town of Fremont, Indiana, shall burn any rubbish except in metal or masonry
burning container being completely enclosed with 3/4-inch openings in the top
of the container and 3/4-inch openings on the sides of the container.
   (B)   While the rubbish is being burned, the metal or masonry burning
container shall not be located or situated closer than 20 feet from any
building, whether the building be a dwelling, commercial or storage structure.
(1996 Code, § 6-22) Penalty, see §
91.999
§ 91.017 ENFORCEMENT.
   (A)   The enforcement of this subchapter shall be by the Town Council of the
Town of Fremont, Indiana.
   (B)   (1)   The Town of Fremont, Indiana, may enforce the provisions of this
subchapter by injunction proceedings or by penalties hereinafter provided.
      (2)   In the event that injunction proceedings are instituted, the cost
thereof including attorney fees shall be paid by the individual person or
corporation violating the provisions of this subchapter.
(1996 Code, § 6-23)
§ 91.018 FIRE LIMITS ESTABLISHED.
   The following fire limits are established within the corporate limits of the
town: beginning at the intersection of Albion Street and Tolford center line of
Tolford Street, also know as Broad Street, to the intersection of Tolford
Street with Spring Street; thence east on the center line of Spring Street with
Pleasant Street; thence south on the center line of Pleasant Street to the
intersection of Pleasant Street with Albion Street; thence west on the center
line on Albion Street to the place of beginning.
(1996 Code, § 6-38)
§ 91.019 NON-COMBUSTIBLE MATERIAL REQUIRED.
   Any new building erected or additions made to buildings already within the
fire zone, shall be of non-combustible material as approved by the State Fire
Code.
(1996 Code, § 6-39) Penalty, see §
91.999
§ 91.020 PROHIBITED ACTIONS.
   (A)   It is made unlawful for any person or persons to remove any wooden
frame or other building, the outer walls and roof of which are not made and
constructed of some non-combustible material, from any point without the fire
limits to any point within the fire limits, or from any point within the fire
limits to any other point within the fire limits.
   (B)   It shall be unlawful for any person to kindle or maintain any bonfire
or knowingly furnish the materials for any fire or to authorize or direct any
fire to be kindled or maintained at any place within the fire zone, except in a
properly installed stove, incinerator, fireplace, furnace or safely constructed
enclosure of 1/4-inch mesh wire, or similar safety device.
(1996 Code, § 6-40) Penalty, see §
91.999
§ 91.021 OPEN BURNING.
   (A)   No person shall kindle or maintain any open fire, or burn any
materials including leaves, trash, refuse, rubbish, debris, construction
materials or any other materials, whether organic or inorganic, within the town
limits of the Town of Fremont, Indiana.
   (B)   This section shall not prohibit the maintenance of an outdoor fire for
cooking or recreational purposes provided that the fire is adequately confined
to a reasonable level using appropriate restraining apparatus for that purpose,
the fire is located no closer than 20 feet from any structure, and provided
that the fire is supervised at all times by 1 or more persons over the age of
18.
   (C)   Notwithstanding the prohibitions established by divisions (A) and (B)
above, the following types of open burning shall be permitted only with the
prior approval of the Chief of the Fremont Volunteer Fire Department or its
successor entity:
      (1)   Bonfires used for the purpose of celebrating school pep rallies;
      (2)   Bonfires used for the purpose of celebrating community events;
      (3)   Emergency burning of spilled petroleum products when all reasonable
efforts to recover the spilled material have been exhausted and failure to burn
materials would result in an imminent fire hazard or pollution of waterways;
      (4)   Burning of refuse resulting from a natural disaster;
      (5)   Burning for the purpose of fire training; and
      (6)   Operation of a municipal burning pit by the Town of Fremont,
Indiana.
   (D)   (1)   The express or implied repeal or amendment by this section of
any other section or division of any other section does not affect any rights
or liabilities accrued, penalties incurred or procedures begun prior to the
effective date of this section.
      (2)   Those rights, liabilities and proceedings are continued, and
penalties shall be imposed and enforced under the repealed or amended section
as if this section had not been adopted.
(Ord. 2003-04, passed 6-9-2003) Penalty, see §
91.999
§ 91.022 LOCAL DISASTER EMERGENCY BURN BAN.
   (A)   Title. This section shall be known as the Local Disaster Emergency
Burn Ban ordinance of the town and shall apply to the entire incorporated area
of the town. The mandatory provisions of this section and of any local disaster
emergency burn ban issued pursuant to this section, including the prohibitions
of certain burnings and the penalties for violating those prohibitions, shall
only apply to incorporated areas maintained by the town.
   (B)   Procedure.
      (1)   The principal executive officer, as defined in §
30.11 may declare a local disaster emergency burn ban, in the principal
executive officer's judgment, when such order would be appropriate under I.C.
10-14-3-29 and in the best interest of the public safety and welfare of the
residents of the town.
      (2)   Pursuant to I.C. 10-14-3-29, a declaration for a local disaster
emergency burn ban shall continue in effect for no longer than 7 days, except
with the consent of the Town Council that the local disaster emergency shall
last longer than 7 days. The local disaster emergency burn ban shall continue
until the principal executive officer, or the Town Council if applicable,
declares the emergency no longer exists and terminates the emergency order.
   (C)   Declaration. A local disaster emergency burn ban shall be declared in
accordance with I.C. 10-14-3-29 and this section. The purpose of a local
disaster emergency burn ban is to keep the residents of the town informed of
the increased risk of fire danger due to dry weather conditions and to prohibit
certain burnings in order to protect the well being of the citizens and
property within the town.
   (D)   Prohibited burnings.
      (1)   Unless otherwise set forth herein, while a local disaster emergency
burn ban is in effect, the following burnings shall be prohibited within the
entire incorporated area of the town: (i) the burning of unattended campfires;
(ii) the burning of brush; (iii) the burning of trash fires; (iv) the burning
of articles within burn barrels; and (v) the burning of any other open air
fires, including the use of fireworks. The use of a gas or charcoal grill is
permissible and shall not be considered a violation of this section.
      (2)   Pursuant to I.C. 22-11-14-10.5, while a local disaster emergency
burn ban is in effect, the use of fireworks shall only be permitted during the
following periods: (i) between the hours of 5:00 p.m. and 2 hours after sunset
on June 29, June 30, July 1, July 2, July 3, July 5, July 6, July 7, July 8,
and July 9; (ii) between the hours of 10:00 a.m. and 12:00 midnight on July 4;
and (iii) between the hours of 10:00 a.m. on December 31 and 1:00 a.m. on
January 1.
   (E)   Publication. Any order or proclamation declaring, continuing, or
terminating a local disaster emergency burn ban shall be given prompt and
general publicity and shall be filed promptly in the office of the Clerk-
Treasurer pursuant to I.C. 10-14-3-22(b)(2). Publication and broadcast of a
local disaster emergency burn ban shall be made or caused to be made by the
principal executive officer or other officials designating the local disaster
emergency burn ban by a press release to all law enforcement agencies, fire
departments, hospitals, and news media in the town.
(Ord. 2012-06, passed 7-5-2012) Penalty, see §
91.999
SANITARY REGULATIONS
§ 91.065 COMPLIANCE WITH STATE BOARD OF HEALTH.
   Every inhabitable dwelling, business house, boarding house, lodging house,
eating place, tenement, shop, factory, public hall, place of amusement and all
public buildings in the town shall be provided with a sanitary toilet of
sufficient size and construction to meet the full requirements of the rules of
the State Board of Health.
(1996 Code, § 6-71)
§ 91.066 REQUIREMENTS.
   Where at any time there shall be maintained, established or installed a
privy, the privy shall be so constructed or built and maintained in a manner so
as to meet the recommendations for construction and maintenance for sanitary
privies as set forth by the Bureau of Sanitary Engineering of the State Board
of Health, as may be amended from time to time.
(1996 Code, § 6-72) Penalty, see §
91.999
§ 91.067 JUNK YARDS PROHIBITED.
   It shall be unlawful for any person, persons, corporation, partnership or
individual to own, operate or maintain, within the corporate limits of the Town
of Fremont, Steuben County, Indiana, any junk yards of any kind, nature or
character for the storage of refuse or garbage.
(1996 Code, § 6-84) Penalty, see §
91.999
§ 91.068 UNLICENSED VEHICLES.
   It shall also be unlawful to store any unlicensed motor vehicle, motor parts
or repair parts, machinery upon any lot or lots in the Town of Fremont, Steuben
County, Indiana, unless it shall be operated by a licensed automobile or
machinery dealer in the State of Indiana, and shall be subject to the
provisions of this code.
(1996 Code, § 6-85) Penalty, see §
91.999
MISCELLANEOUS REGULATIONS
§ 91.080 DISCHARGE OF FIREARMS AND THROWING OF MISSILES.
   (A)   Subject to the provisions of division (B) below, no person shall
knowingly discharge a firearm or throw a missile within the corporate limits of
the Town of Fremont.
   (B)   Division (A) above shall not be applicable to:
      (1)   Federal, state or local law enforcement officers, while acting in
furtherance of their law enforcement duties;
      (2)   Authorized persons appropriately using an interior firing range
designed and certified as being in compliance with Indiana state police, the
NRA or a state regulatory agency, and which is designed to and does preclude
the discharge from being audible on any adjacent property; or
      (3)   A person who acts within the permissible limits of self-defense and
defense of others, as described by I.C. 35-41-3-2 and the laws and statutes of
the State of Indiana.
   (C)   For the purpose of this subchapter, the following definitions shall
apply unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
      FIREARMS. Any weapon or device that has the capacity to, is designed to,
or that may readily be converted to expel a projectile by means of an
explosion.
      KNOWINGLY. A person engages in conduct "knowingly" when he or she is
aware of a high probability that he or she is discharging a firearm or throwing
a missile.
      MISSILE. Any weapon or object designed or used for throwing, hurling,
launching, or shooting, including, but not limited to, a stone, bullet, bolt or
arrow.
   (D)   (1)   Any person who knowingly violates Division (A) shall be fined
not more than $25 for each violation.
      (2)   No parent, guardian or other person having legal control of any
person less than 18 years of age, shall permit the minor to violate this
section. Any parent, guardian or other person having legal custody of a minor
person shall be liable for any fine assessed due to the minor's violation of
this subchapter.
(Ord. 2016-13, passed - -)
§ 91.081 LOITERING PROHIBITED.
   (A)   (1)   A person shall not stand, lie, lounge or sit (either directly or
on a chair, box or other object) on any street, alley, sidewalk, curb, gutter,
any public right-of-way or in any driveway open to the public or in any
doorway, entranceway or passageway affording entrance or exit by the public
into or from any building, regardless of whether the building or any
establishment therein is open for business or not. Nor shall a person
congregate with others in such places so as to physically obstruct by his or
her actions or behavior, presence or location, unimpeded passage by others.
      (2)   A person shall not sit, stand, lie or lounge upon, or hang upon or
from the exterior of any automobile, bus, truck, motor vehicle or vehicular
trailer (except in the cargo or passenger seats or compartments thereof),
whether the vehicle is moving, stopped or parked, in such a manner so as to
physically obstruct by his or her actions or behavior, presence or location,
unimpeded passage by others.
      (3)   A person shall not cause, or incite by illegal activities,
arguments or disturbances, or use abusive or obscene language disturbing others
within the business sections of the town.
      (4)   The prohibition, above, against sitting on the sidewalk shall not
apply to a bona fide vendor of newspapers who has in his or her immediate
possession current newspapers being offered for sale by him or her to the
general public and who is not obstructing passage by others.
      (5)   The prohibition, above, against sitting on the sidewalk and curbs
shall not apply during or immediately prior to any public parade or other
public celebration at the site of such parade or celebration for which parade
or celebration the proper governmental agency has granted permission.
      (6)   The prohibition against sitting on sidewalks shall not apply to
personnel of business establishments who, during a sidewalk sale for which a
proper permit has been granted by the Town, are sitting on chairs or benches on
the sidewalk adjacent to the establishment during the sale.
      (7)   The Town Council is empowered to suspend the provisions of this
section, or particular prohibitions hereof, generally or in certain areas only,
when, in connection with carnivals, public activities, and other public events,
such suspension is warranted in the opinion and discretion of the Town Council.
No such suspension shall be for a period of longer than 8 consecutive days
without a separate resolution of the Town Council for each period.
      (8)   Each Marshal of the Town is authorized to enforce the prohibitions
of this section by issuing a traffic summons to any offender seen by such
officer in violation of this section. However, a violation who is not a
resident in the state may be required to post bond, not to exceed $100,
notwithstanding his or her written promise to appear in court.
   (B)   (1)   It is unlawful for any person, firm, corporation, association or
company to erect, establish, situate or maintain any type of mailbox upon any
highway, state or county, any street, alley or sidewalk running through or in
the Town of Fremont for the purpose of having mail delivered thereto by the
Post Office Department without the express written approval of the Postmaster
of the Fremont Post Office and the Fremont Town Council.
      (2)   Any person or individual as described in division (B)(1) above
having violated this division shall be given written notice by the Town of
Fremont, Indiana, to remove the same within 5 days after the receipt of notice,
the Town of Fremont, Indiana, is authorized to remove the mailbox from the
highway, street, alley or sidewalk and the cost thereof shall be assessed
against the individual. The town shall use all legal means at its disposal to
collect the costs of removal.
(1996 Code, § 6-94)
§ 91.082 DEFINITIONS.
   Public nuisances are defined in accordance with I.C. 36-8-2-4 and may
include but shall not be limited to the following:
   (A)   Litter,
   (B)   Grass and weeds;
   (C)   Boxes, appliances, furniture, household items, automobile parts or any
other property or items, which have accumulated outside a home, or on a vacant
lot, or a business or any other place within the Town of Fremont;
   (D)   Demolition and/or construction remains;
   (E)   Accumulated garbage and trash;
   (F)   Structures defaced with paint or graffiti or in any other way caused
to become unsightly;
   (G)   The placing or accumulating on or within any real or personal property
or the permitting of same, of any material which attracts or may attract
rodents, insects, domestic or wild animals in a manner so as to create a health
hazard or unsanitary or dangerous condition;
   (H)   Trees, shrubbery, weeds or other matter obstructing public ways, or
causing visual bathers which create vehicular traffic or pedestrian safety
hazards;
   (I)   The unauthorized placement of fences, signs, shrubbery or any other
thing within the road rights-of-way;
   (J)   (1)   Noxious odors or smoke.
      (2)   If there emits from premises into the surrounding atmosphere like
odors, dust, smoke or other matter as to render ordinary use, or physical
occupation of other property in the vicinity uncomfortable or impossible; and
   (K)   Noise. If there emits from premises noise noxious enough to destroy
the enjoyment of dwelling houses or other uses of property in the vicinity by
interfering with ordinary comforts of human existence.
(1996 Code, § 6-95)
§ 91.083 TEST FOR NUISANCE.
   Whether or not a particular annoyance, of the character listed in §
91.082 constitutes a nuisance shall depend upon its effect upon persons of
ordinary health and average sensibilities.
(1996 Code, § 6-96)
§ 91.084 CLEANLINESS OF PREMISES GENERALLY.
   (A)   All persons owning or controlling houses or premises or vacant lots
within the Town of Fremont, shall maintain the premises in a reasonably clean
and orderly manner and to a standard conforming generally to other orderly
premises in that vicinity.
   (B)   It shall be a violation of this section to abandon, neglect or
disregard any premises so as to permit the same to be considered a public
nuisance as defined in §
91.082.
(1996 Code, § 6-97)
§ 91.085 DUTY OF OWNER OR PERSON IN CONTROL OF PREMISES.
   No persons owning or controlling any premises in the town shall allow a
public nuisance as defined in §
91.082 to remain or exist thereon or permit the same to become unsightly,
unsanitary or obnoxious, a blight to the vicinity or offensive to the senses of
users of the public way abutting the same, for a period longer than 30 days in
any calendar year or a shorter period of time as may be required because of an
emergency or dangerous condition; or fail to comply with these requirements
after a written order from any officer of the town including but not limited to
police officers, the Town Manager or any other employee of the town authorized
by the Town Council to police like matters.
(1996 Code, § 6-98) Penalty, see §
91.999
§ 91.086 REQUIREMENTS OF NOTICE.
   (A)   The notice to abate the nuisance shall be delivered in a manner so as
to assure receipt by the responsible party.
   (B)   The notice shall include the following information:
      (1)   The name of the person to whom the order is issued;
      (2)   The address and a brief description of the property that is the
subject of the notice;
      (3)   The action that the notice requires the person to perform;
      (4)   The period of time in which the action is to be accomplished,
beginning the day after service of the notice has been accomplished; and
      (5)   A statement that failure to comply with the notice could result in
a remedial order and/or penalties as provided in the town code.
(1996 Code, § 6-99)
§ 91.087 COSTS OF ABATEMENT BY TOWN.
   (A)   If the person to whom the notice is issued fails to abate the nuisance
or in any other way fails to comply with the notice, the town may take action
as is necessary to abate the nuisance and the costs of abating the nuisance
shall be charged to the person to whom the notice is issued, or to anyone who
has a substantial property interest in the property.
   (B)   (1)   Upon abatement of the nuisance by the town, the Clerk-Treasurer
shall make a certified statement of the actual cost incurred by the town in the
abatement, which certified statement shall include administrative expenses.
      (2)   The certified statement shall be delivered to the owner, lessee or
occupier of the real estate or property by registered mail.
      (3)   If the responsible party fails to pay the amount certified on the
statement within 10 days after receipt of the statement, a certified copy of
the statement shall be filed in the office of the auditor of Steuben County,
and the amount contained thereon shall be added to the tax duplicate of the
property effected by the work.
(1996 Code, § 6-100)
§ 91.088 CLEARING OF SNOW AND ICE REQUIRED.
   (A)   (1)   The occupant of occupied premises and the owner of unoccupied
premises or vacant lot situated in the town are required to keep the sidewalks
in front of or adjacent to the premises free from snow and ice, as provided in
this section.
      (2)   OCCUPANT, as used in this section, shall mean the person occupying,
for business, as a residence, or for other purposes, the first floor of any
building situated on the premises.
      (3)   If the first floor of any building is not occupied, then the
premises shall be deemed and held to be unoccupied, and the owner thereof shall
be required to keep the sidewalks in front of or adjacent thereto free from
snow and ice.
   (B)   In case any snow or ice accumulated on any sidewalk as described in
division (A) above has not been removed by the occupant or owner within 24
hours from the time the snow ceased to fall or the ice has accumulated, then in
either of those cases the occupant or owner shall be deemed and held to have
violated the provisions of this section.
   (C)   (1)   All businesses open to the public shall remove all snow or ice
accumulated on any sidewalk within 2 hours from the time the snow ceased to
fall or the ice has accumulated, unless that occurs during non-business hours,
in which case the snow and ice shall be removed within 2 hours after the start
of business.
      (2)   Should the provisions of this division (C) not apply for any
reason, nevertheless, business owners shall be subject to all other provisions
of this section.
   (D)   Any person charged with violation of this subchapter whether by
ticket, citation or affidavit, shall have the option of paying the fine imposed
within the time specified in the notice of arrest at the Town Clerk-Treasurer’s
office on entering a plea of guilty and on waiving appearance in court.
   (E)   The payment of a fine to the Clerk-Treasurer shall be deemed an
acknowledgment of conviction of the alleged offense, and the Clerk-Treasurer,
on accepting the prescribed fine, shall issue a receipt to the violator as
acknowledging payment therefore.
   (F)   If any owner, occupant or business as described in this section does
not remove the snow and ice as provided, the Street Superintendent is
authorized to remove or cause to be removed the snow and ice, and report, in
writing, the necessary expense incident thereto to the Clerk-Treasurer, who
shall certify the amount, with a description of the lot or parcel or ground and
the owner's name the amount shall then become a lien on the lot or parcel of
ground, and shall be collected by the Clerk-Treasurer at the same time and in
the same manner that the other assessments on real estate are collected.
(1996 Code, § 6-101)
WEEDS
§ 91.100 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this subchapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   NOXIOUS WEEDS. Includes the following NOXIOUS WEEDS: Canada thistle, Johnson
grass and Sorghum album, Bur cucumber, Shattercane, Poison ivy, Poison sumac,
Poison oak, Quackgrass, Carolina horsenettle, Cocklebur, Wild mustard, Jimson,
Burdock, Ragweed, Thistle, and Indian or Wild Hemp.
   RANK VEGETATION. Any plant exceeding 6 inches in height. Trees, shrubberies,
flowers, ornamental grasses, and agricultural crops exceeding 6 inches are not
to be considered RANK VEGETATION unless they constitute an extreme deviation
from the aesthetic appearance of the real estate within the Town of Fremont.
   WETLANDS.  A swampy or marshy area and include the areas immediately
surrounding ponds, riverbeds, and streams.
   WOODED AREAS.  An area densely covered with trees and shrubs.
(Ord. 2006-19, passed 9-19-2006)
§ 91.101 EXCLUSIONS.
   This subchapter shall not apply to:
   (A)   Wooded areas;
   (B)   Wetlands;
   (C)   Wildlife projects conducted and funded by educational institutions or
local, state or federal government entities; or
   (D)   Hay fields and pastures.
(Ord. 2006-19, passed 9-19-2006)
§ 91.102 REMOVAL REQUIREMENTS.
   (A)   Rank vegetation: The owners of real estate located within the Town of
Fremont shall cut or remove rank vegetation from an area within the public
right-of-way, within 150 feet of an adjacent real estate owner or within 150
feet of a public right-of-way.
   (B)   Noxious weeds: The owners of real estate located within the Town of
Fremont shall remove and eliminate all noxious weeds.
(Ord. 2006-19, passed 9-19-2006)
§ 91.103 NOTIFICATION.
   An owner of real estate within the Town of Fremont or resident of the Town
of Fremont may file a written complaint with the Clerk-Treasurer or Town
Manager. The Town Manager shall investigate the complaint. If the Town
Manager's investigation indicates that there is a violation of this subchapter
significant enough to warrant enforcement, the Town Manager or Clerk-Treasurer
will issue a notice to the owner in accordance with §
91.104. The Town may initiate an enforcement action on its own without a
complaint being filed with the Clerk-Treasurer or Town Manger if the Town
becomes aware of a violation of this subchapter which the Town believes is
significant enough to warrant enforcement.
(Ord. 2006-19, passed 9-19-2006)
§ 91.104 REMOVAL TIME.
   Upon discovering a parcel of real estate containing rank vegetation or
noxious weeds, the Town Manager or Clerk-Treasurer shall give the owner of the
real estate a written notice to cut and remove the rank vegetation or remove
and eliminate the noxious weeds. The owner shall have 5 business days to abate
the violation from the real estate. Service of this notice is adequate if given
to the owner of the real estate in person or sent by first-class mail, postage
prepaid, to the owner at the address listed with the County Auditor's office.
(Ord. 2006-19, passed 9-19-2006)
§ 91.105 REMOVAL BY TOWN.
   Should any person who has been provided written notice fail, neglect or
refuse to cut or remove the rank vegetation and/or fail, neglect or refuse to
remove and eliminate the noxious weeds from the real estate within 5 business
days as required by the notice, the town may retain the services of a person or
business to enter upon the premises and cause the rank vegetation to be cut or
removed and/or cause the noxious weeds to be removed and eliminated.
(Ord. 2006-19, passed 9-19-2006)
§ 91.106 COST OF REMOVAL.
   In the event the Town is forced to cut or remove rank vegetation and/or
remove and eliminate-the noxious weeds, the Clerk-Treasurer shall issue a bill
to the owner of the real estate for $75 or the actual cost of the abatement, if
greater. The Clerk-Treasurer shall keep record of the billing and collect the
same as the Clerk-Treasurer does other charges of the town. Payment shall be
due to the Clerk-Treasurer's Office 15 days after the bill is mailed to the
owner.
(Ord. 2006-19, passed 9-19-2006)
§ 91.107 CERTIFICATION OF COST.
   If the owner fails to pay the bill within 15 days, the Town may collect the
bill in any manner available at law. The Clerk-Treasurer may also certify to
the County Auditor the amount of the bill plus any additional administrative
costs incurred in the certification. The Auditor shall place the total amount
certified on the tax duplicate for the property affected, and the total amount,
including any accrued interest, shall be collected as delinquent taxes and
shall be disbursed to the general fund of the town as provided by I.C. 36-7-
10.1-4.
(Ord. 2006-19, passed 9-19-2006)
§ 91.108 APPEAL PROCESS.
   (A)   A person may appeal a notice of violation issued pursuant to this
subchapter or a bill issued pursuant to this subchapter by submitting a
request, in writing, to the Clerk-Treasurer. The request must be received by
the Clerk-Treasurer within the amount of time set out in the notice of
violation or within 15 days of the date the bill was issued. A hearing before
the Town Council to dispute the existence of a violation or dispute the
accuracy of a bill issued will be scheduled.
   (B)   At the hearing before the Town Council, the person receiving a notice
of violation will be given the opportunity to appear, with or without counsel,
to present such evidence to the Town Council. Each person appearing shall have
the opportunity to cross-examine those persons establishing the violation for
the town, and testify on their own behalf.
   (C)   At the hearing the Town Council shall enter a finding determining
whether the party notified is the owner of the real estate; and whether the
condition of the real estate is in violation of this subchapter or whether the
bill issued is accurate. The Town Council may affirm or modify the notice of
violation consistent with the Town Council's findings. All findings by the Town
Council shall be deemed conclusive.
(Ord. 2006-19, passed 9-19-2006)
§ 91.109 AFFECT.
   The express or implied repeal or amendment by this subchapter of any other
subchapter or part of any other subchapter does not affect any rights or
liabilities accrued, penalties incurred, or procedures begun prior to the
effective date of this subchapter. Those rights, liabilities, and proceedings
are continued, and penalties shall be imposed and enforced under the repealed
or amended subchapter as if this subchapter had not been adopted.
(Ord. 2006-19, passed 9-19-2006)
§ 91.110 CONFLICT OF LAW.
   No part of this subchapter shall be interpreted to conflict with any local,
state or federal laws, and all reasonable efforts should be made to harmonize
