same. Should any section or part thereof of this subchapter be declared by a
court of competent jurisdiction to be invalid, such decision shall not affect
the validity of the subchapter as a whole, or any other portion there-of other
than that portion so declared to be invalid, and for this purpose the
provisions of this subchapter are hereby declared to be severable.
(Ord. 2006-19, passed 9-19-2006)
§ 91.999 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no
specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99.
   (B)   Any persons violating any provision of §
91.022 shall be guilty of the commission of an infraction and may be fined any
sum not to exceed $100, and such shall be enforceable in any court of law, duly
authorized by state law, and in addition to such fine the court shall be
authorized to direct the violator to repay the town any monetary losses or
expenses incurred in the incident.
(Ord. 2012-06, passed 7-5-2012)
CHAPTER 92: ANIMALS
Section
   
92.01   Control over animals
   
92.02   Certain animals prohibited
   
92.03   Harboring noisy animals prohibited
   
92.04   Running at large
   
92.05   Impounding; destroying dogs or animals
   
92.06   Authority
   
92.07   Sanitation procedures
   
92.99   Penalty
§ 92.01 CONTROL OVER ANIMALS.
   The town may regulate the control of animals, and may establish animal
shelters.
(1996 Code, § 6-5)
§ 92.02 CERTAIN ANIMALS PROHIBITED.
   It shall be unlawful for any person, firm or corporation to house, keep or
harbor cattle, sheep, hogs or any fowl within the corporate limits of the town.
(1996 Code, § 6-9) Penalty, see §
92.99
§ 92.03 HARBORING NOISY ANIMALS PROHIBITED.
   (A)   It shall be unlawful for any person knowingly to keep or harbor any
dog or other type domestic animal which habitually barks, howls, yelps, cries
or makes any other type noise to the great discomfort of the peace and quiet of
the neighborhood, or in a manner so as to materially disturb or annoy persons
in the neighborhood who are of ordinary sensibilities.
   (B)   These dogs and other type of animals are declared to be a public
nuisance.
(1996 Code, § 6-10) Penalty, see §
92.99
§ 92.04 RUNNING AT LARGE.
   It is unlawful for the owner or keeper of a dog or other domestic animal to
permit the dog or animal to roam the streets, alleys or other public places of
the town unless under the personal control and custody of the owner, or some
individual authorized to be in charge by the owner, secured by a leash or reins
or a dog or domestic animal trained to respond to voice command and reasonably
expected to obey voice command.
(1996 Code, § 6-11) Penalty, see §
92.99
§ 92.05 IMPOUNDING; DESTROYING DOGS OR ANIMALS.
   (A)   The Town Marshal or any deputy thereof is authorized to seize, hold
for impounding or destroy any unlicensed, vicious or stray dog, and any vicious
or stray domestic animal, if the dog or animal is found in any public place in
the town or upon any premises other than those occupied or owned by the owner
of the dog.
   (B)   This authority includes, but is not limited to the authority to use
tranquilizer guns or where appropriate lethal weapons.
(1996 Code, § 6-12) Penalty, see §
92.99
§ 92.06 AUTHORITY.
   The provisions of §§
92.04 through
92.06 are to be in addition to the provisions of any other ordinance or
statute, and the authority granted by this chapter is in addition to the
authority granted by any other ordinance or statute.
(1996 Code, § 6-13) Penalty, see §
92.99
§ 92.07 SANITATION PROCEDURES.
   (A)   No owner or custodian of any animal shall cause or allow an animal to
soil, defile or defecate on any public property or upon any street, sidewalk,
public way, play area or common grounds owned jointly by the members of a
homeowners or condominium association, or upon private property other than that
of the owner, unless the owner or custodian immediately removes and disposes of
all feces deposited by an animal by the following methods:
      (1)   Collection of the feces by appropriate implement and placement in a
paper or plastic bag or container;
      (2)   Removal of the bag or container to the property of the animal owner
or custodian or disposition in garbage bins, not storm drains or drainage
ditches or any other public or private property except private property owned
by the owner or custodian; and
      (3)   The owner or agent walking his or her dog or other animal outside
of his or her private property must have in his or her possession a pooper
scooper, plastic bag or similar devise to pick up the dog's excrement if
deposited while on the walk.
   (B)   No person owning, harboring or keeping an animal within the town shall
permit any waste matter from the animal to collect or remain on the property of
the owner or custodian, or on the property of others so as to cause or create
an unhealthy, unsanitary, dangerous or offensive living condition on the
owner's or custodian's property, or to abutting property of others.
   (C)   No person owning, harboring, keeping or in charge of any animal shall
cause unsanitary dangerous or offensive conditions by virtue of the size or
number of animals maintained at a single location or due to the inadequacy of
the facilities.
   (D)   Guide dogs for the blind are exempt.
(1996 Code, § 6-15) Penalty, see §
92.99
§ 92.99 PENALTY.
   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no specific
penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99.
CHAPTER 93: ABANDONED AND JUNK VEHICLES
Section
   
93.01   Adoption of state law
   
93.02   Abandoned Vehicle Fund established
   
93.03   Notice of violation
   
93.04   Emergency situations
   
93.05   Vehicle removal
   
93.06   Notification of towing
   
93.07   Fees
   
93.08   Sale of abandoned vehicles
   
93.09   Abandoned vehicles on private property
   
93.10   Disposal of vehicles
   
93.11   Liens
   
93.12   Waiver of responsibility
§ 93.01 ADOPTION OF STATE LAW.
   All of the power, purpose, provisions and definitions (I.C. 9-22-1 et seq.
and I.C. 9-13-2 et seq.) contained in such “Abandoned Vehicle Act” are now
incorporated by reference in this chapter and made a part thereof.
(Ord. 2007-06, passed 6-9-2007)
§ 93.02 ABANDONED VEHICLE FUND ESTABLISHED.
   The town hereby establishes the Abandoned Vehicle Fund (the “Fund”). The
Town Council may appropriate sufficient money to the Fund to carry out the
purposes of this chapter. All revenue received and all costs of implementation
of the chapter shall be deposited to or credited against the Fund. All money
remaining in the Fund at the end of the year shall remain in the Fund and this
Fund shall not revert to the General Fund.
(Ord. 2007-06, passed 6-9-2007)
§ 93.03 NOTICE OF VIOLATION.
   A law enforcement officer who finds or is notified of a vehicle, or parts of
a vehicle, within the jurisdictional limits of the town believed to be
abandoned shall post a notice on the vehicle stating:
   (A)   Time and date, officer's name, public agency, and the address and
telephone number to contact for further information;
   (B)   Notice that the vehicle or parts thereof will be removed after 72
hours.
   (C)   Notice that the person who owns the vehicle will be held responsible
for the costs incidental to the removal, storage, and disposal of the vehicle.
   (D)   Notice that the vehicle or parts are considered abandoned.
   (E)   Notice that the person who owns the vehicle may avoid costs by
removing the vehicle or parts within 72 hours.
(Ord. 2007-06, passed 6-9-2007)
§ 93.04 EMERGENCY SITUATIONS.
   When an abandoned vehicle creates an emergency situation, the vehicle may be
removed immediately. “Emergency Situation” means that the presence of the
vehicle interferes physically with the conduct of normal business operations of
the person who owns or controls the private property or poses a threat to the
safety or security of persons or property, or both.
(Ord. 2007-06, passed 6-9-2007)
§ 93.05 VEHICLE REMOVAL.
   (A)   Any vehicle or vehicle parts, which have not been removed within 72
hours of placement of the notice on it, shall be towed, at the owner's expense,
to a reasonable location for storage and stored, at the owner's expense.
   (B)   Before the towing of the vehicle, an officer shall prepare a report
for the town and take photographs of the vehicle or vehicle parts.
   (C)   The report shall describe the abandoned vehicle or parts, including
make, model, vehicle identification number, license plate number and a
description of the vehicle.
   (D)   The report shall include information on the condition of the vehicle,
including missing parts, damage, and other facts that might substantiate the
estimated market value of the vehicle or parts. Photographs shall be taken to
describe the condition of the vehicle or parts.
   (E)   The report shall also request from the Indiana Bureau of Motor
Vehicles the name and contact information for the owner and any person or
business who holds a lien on the vehicle.
   (F)   The report and photographs of the vehicle shall be maintained by the
town and filed with the Indiana Bureau of Motor Vehicles with 72 hours after
removal.
(Ord. 2007-06, passed 6-9-2007)
§ 93.06 NOTIFICATION OF TOWING.
   (A)   The town, after taking custody of the abandoned vehicle and parts and
filing the report with the Indiana Bureau of Motor Vehicles, will attempt to
notify the owner and any lienholder of the location of the vehicle or parts.
   (B)   Within 72 hours after removal of a vehicle to a storage yard or towing
service, the town or towing service shall conduct a search of national
databases, including a database of vehicle identification numbers, to attempt
to obtain the name and address of the person who owns or holds a lien on the
vehicle.
   (C)   If the town obtains the name and address of the person who owns or
holds a lien on the vehicle, within 72 hours after obtaining the name and
address, the town shall, by certified mail, notify the owner or lien holder of
the name, address, and telephone number of the town.
(Ord. 2007-06, passed 6-9-2007)
§ 93.07 FEES.
   (A)   The town shall charge the owner of the abandoned vehicle or parts the
actual cost of towing and the actual storage fee, which will accrue daily, plus
any costs of disposition.
   (B)   The owner of the abandoned vehicle shall be responsible for paying the
town all of the above fees, up to a maximum amount of $1,500, before recovering
possession of the vehicle or parts from the town.
(Ord. 2007-06, passed 6-9-2007)
§ 93.08 SALE OF ABANDONED VEHICLES.
   (A)   The owner of an abandoned vehicle shall have 20 days, from the date of
the notice referenced in §
93.06, to pay the towing fee and accrued storage fees for the vehicle and to
recover possession of the vehicles taken into custody by the town.
   (B)   If the owner of an abandoned vehicle does not pay the towing fees,
storage fees, and recover possession of the abandoned vehicle within the 20
days provided in division (A), the town may sell the vehicle in any
commercially reasonable manner, and the owner of the vehicle shall be
responsible for any and all costs incurred by the town in selling the abandoned
vehicle.
   (C)   (1)   Upon selling the abandoned vehicle, the town will apply the
proceeds from the sale of the abandoned vehicle to the fees it incurred to tow
and store the vehicle, as well as any other costs and expenses associated with
selling the vehicle.
      (2)   A statement of the sale proceeds shall be sent to the owner of the
abandoned vehicle that describes the application of said proceeds to fees,
costs and other expenses.
      (3)   If the proceeds of the sale of the abandoned vehicle do not
adequately compensate the town, then the town may sue the owner of the
abandoned vehicle to obtain the remainder of the outstanding fees.
      (4)   If the proceeds from the sale exceed the costs, fees, and expenses,
the town shall forward any remaining proceeds to the previous owner of the
vehicle or lienholder.
(Ord. 2007-06, passed 6-9-2007)
§ 93.09 ABANDONED VEHICLES ON PRIVATE PROPERTY.
   (A)   In the event that an abandoned vehicle is on private property, the
town, upon being notified by the owner of the real property on which an
abandoned vehicle has remained for a period of at least 72 hours, shall place
notice upon said abandoned vehicle or parts.
   (B)   If after 72 hours the vehicle has not been removed, the town or person
who owns or controls the private property may have the vehicle towed from the
private property. The officer shall prepare a report with photographs of the
abandoned vehicles or parts and otherwise follow the procedures provided above.
(Ord. 2007-06, passed 6-9-2007)
§ 93.10 DISPOSAL OF VEHICLES.
   (A)   Notwithstanding any provision to the contrary, if the officer
reasonably determines the fair market value of the abandoned vehicle or parts
is less than $500, then the town will immediately dispose of the abandoned
vehicle to a storage yard, for sale not less than 30 days after the date on
which the towing service removed the abandoned vehicle.
   (B)   A copy of the abandoned vehicle report and photographs relating to the
abandoned vehicle shall be forwarded to the Indiana Bureau of Motor Vehicles.
   (C)   The town after disposing of the vehicle shall retain the original
records and photographs for at least 2 years.
(Ord. 2007-06, passed 6-9-2007)
§ 93.11 LIENS.
   If the owner or the holder of a lien on an abandoned vehicle or parts cannot
be identified due to the condition of the abandoned vehicle or parts, then the
abandoned vehicle may be disposed of without notice.
(Ord. 2007-06, passed 6-9-2007)
§ 93.12 WAIVER OF RESPONSIBILITY.
   The town, its employees, agents, contractors, officials, officers, towing
service or storage yard shall not be responsible to the owner or any lienholder
of an abandoned vehicle or parts for any damage to the abandoned vehicle
occurring during the removal, storage or disposition of an abandoned vehicle or
parts.
(Ord. 2007-06, passed 6-9-2007)
CHAPTER 94: TREES
Section
   
94.01   Tree Preservation Board
   
94.02   Duties of the Board
   
94.03   Street trees
   
94.04   Tree care
   
94.05   Regulation of tree care
   
94.99   Penalty
§ 94.01 TREE PRESERVATION BOARD.
   (A)   The Street Superintendent shall serve as the Town Forester for the
Town of Fremont.
   (B)   (1)   There is hereby created and established a Town Tree Preservation
Board (Board) for the Town of Fremont consisting of 5 members.
      (2)   The members shall consist of the Town Forester or his or her
designee, 1 member of the Town Council as appointed by the Town Council, 1
member of the Park Board as appointed by the Park Board President and 2 town
residents initially selected from the Tree Ordinance Committee at an open
public meeting.
      (3)   Thereafter, the Town Council shall select 2 town residents for each
subsequent Board.
   (C)   (1)   The term of the Board members shall be 3 years except that the
term of the Park Board and Town Council members appointed to the first Board
shall be for only 1 year.
      (2)   In the event that a vacancy shall occur during the term of any
member, his or her successor shall be appointed by the Town Council for the
unexpired portion of the term.
      (3)   Following expiration of these members’ terms, the positions will be
filled according to procedures established in open public meeting by the Board.
   (D)   Members of the Board shall serve without compensation.
(Ord. 07-2006, passed 4-18-2006)
§ 94.02 DUTIES OF THE BOARD.
   (A)   The Board shall serve in an advisory capacity to the Town Council.
   (B)   The purpose of the Board shall be to promote the responsible planting
of trees on public and private property, public education about trees,
promoting proper maintenance of trees, advocating trees within the town, and
developing innovative and joint funding from a variety of sources.
   (C)   It shall be the responsibility of the Board to study, investigate,
counsel, develop and/or update annually, and administer a written plan for the
care, preservation, pruning, planting and replanting along streets and in other
public areas. The plan will include a tree inventory to be conducted on a
regular basis and updated as tree planting, maintenance and removals are done.
   (D)   The Board shall present the plan annually to the Town Council during
the month of March of each year and upon their acceptance and approval shall
constitute the official comprehensive town tree plan for the Town of Fremont.
   (E)   The Board, when requested by the Town Council, shall consider,
investigate, make a finding, report and recommend upon any special matter of
question coming within the scope of its work.
   (F)   The Board shall choose its own officers, make its own rules and
regulations and keep minutes of its proceedings. A majority of the members
shall be a quorum for the transaction of business. Board will follow the Open
Door Policy and file with the Fremont Clerk-Treasurer the regular annual
meeting schedule in December of the preceding year and all meetings are subject
to 48-hour notice. The minutes of all meetings will be filed with Clerk-
Treasurer as a matter of public record.
(Ord. 07-2006, passed 4-18-2006)
§ 94.03 STREET TREES.
   (A)   For the purpose of this chapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
      STREET TREES. Trees, shrubs, bushes and all other woody vegetation on
land lying between property lines on either side of all streets, highways,
avenues, alleys or ways, or which overhang any streets, highways, avenues,
alleys, sidewalks or ways within the town.
      TREE LAWN. That area of land between a parcel of privately-owned property
and any road, street or highway, but which is actually included within the
road, street or highway right-of-way.
   (B)   The Committee shall recommend to the Town Council the town street tree
planting specifications (specifications). Subject to Town Council approval,
these specifications shall list the official street tree species for the town.
The specifications shall also contain the minimum distances between the trees
and other trees and structures which must be followed for the planting of any
tree under this chapter. The Town Council may amend the specifications from
time to time with advice from the Board.
   (C)   No species other than those included in the specifications may be
planted on the tree lawn without written permission of the Board.
   (D)   The spacing of street trees shall be in accordance with the
specifications, and no trees shall be planted closer to another tree or
structure except as recommended in the specifications unless in special
plantings designed or approved by a landscape architect or forester, and then
approved by the Board.
(Ord. 07-2006, passed 4-18-2006)
§ 94.04 TREE CARE.
   (A)   The town shall have the right to plant, prune, maintain and remove
trees, plants and shrubs which are growing in or overhanging the lines of all
streets, alleys, avenues, lanes, squares and public grounds, as may be
necessary to ensure public safety of public grounds.
   (B)   (1)   The town shall have the right, and may remove or cause or order
to be removed, any tree, plant or shrub or part thereof located on either
public or private property within the town which is in an unsafe condition or
which by reason of its nature is injurious to sewers, electric power lines, gas
lines, water lines or other public improvements, or is affected with any
injurious fungus, insect or other pest and which represents a threat to public
safety.
      (2)   The Board will notify in writing owners of any like trees. Removal
shall be done by the owners at their own expense within 60 days after the date
of the notice. In the event or failure of the owners to comply with the
provisions, the town shall have the authority to remove trees and recover
reasonable expenses incurred in the removal.
   (C)   This section does not prohibit the planting of street trees by
adjacent property owners providing that the selection and location of the trees
is in accordance with this chapter and the specifications developed by the
Board and approved by the Town Council.
   (D)   It shall be unlawful as a normal practice for any person, firm or town
department to top any street tree or other tree on nonpublic property. TOPPING
is defined as the severe cutting back of limbs to stubs larger than 3 inches in
diameter within the tree's crown to a degree so as to remove the normal canopy
and disfigure the tree. Trees severely damaged by storms or other causes, or
certain trees under utility wires or other obstructions where other pruning
practices are impractical may be exempted from this section at the
determination of the Board.
   (E)   (1)   Except as provided in division (F) below, every owner of any
privately-owned tree overhanging any street or right-of-way within the town
shall prune the branches so that the branches shall not obstruct the light from
any street lamp or obstruct the view of any street intersection and so that
there shall be a clear space of 15 feet above the surface of any street or
alley and a clearance space of 8 feet above the surface of any sidewalk.
      (2)   The owner shall remove all dead, diseased or dangerous trees, or
broken or decayed limbs which constitute a menace to the safety of the public.
The town shall have the right to prune or cause to be pruned, any tree or shrub
on the private property when it interferes with the proper spread of light
along the street from a street light or interferes with the visibility of any
traffic control device or sign.
   (F)   (1)   Any tree overhanging the right-of-way of any state road within
the town shall be pruned, cut and maintained by the Indiana Department of
Transportation so that no branches shall obstruct the light from any street
lamp or obstruct the view of any street intersection and so that there shall be
a clear space of 15 feet above the surface of any state highway or right-of-
way.
      (2)   The state shall remove all dead, diseased or dangerous trees, or
broken or decayed limbs which constitute a menace to the safety of the public
which overhang any state road or right of way, and shall have the right to
prune any tree or shrub which overhangs a state road or right-of-way when it
interferes with the proper spread of light along the street from a street light
or interferes with the visibility of any traffic control device or sign even if
the tree or shrub is on private property.
   (G)   No person shall intentionally attach any wire, nails, advertising
posters or other contrivances to any street tree on the tree lawn.
   (H)   No person shall intentionally carve, cut, damage, transplant or remove
any street tree on the tree lawn.
(Ord. 07-2006, passed 4-18-2006) Penalty, see §
94.99
§ 94.05 REGULATION OF TREE CARE.
   (A)   It shall be unlawful for any person to prevent, delay or interfere
with the Board, or any of its agents, while engaging in and about the planting,
cultivating, mulching, pruning, spraying or removing of any street trees or
trees on private grounds, as authorized in this chapter.
   (B)   It shall be unlawful for any person or firm to engage professionally
in the business or occupation of pruning, treating or removing street trees
within the Town of Fremont without first filing evidence of possession of
liability insurance with the Clerk-Treasurer in the minimum amounts of $50,000
for bodily injury and $100,000 for property damage indemnifying the town or any
person injured or damages resulting from the pruning, treating or removing of
street trees.
   (C)   Any town employee doing work in accordance with instructions of his or
her supervisor, the Town Manager or the Town Council shall be exempt from these
regulations but will comply with tree care regulations of this chapter as
standard operating procedure.
   (D)   Any public service company, or company doing work for a public service
company, doing work in the pursuit of their public service endeavors shall
present a plan for pruning, trimming or removal of street trees to the town
forester or his or her designee for approval before beginning work and file
evidence of the plan being approved by a trained arborist.
   (E)   The Town Council shall review the conduct, acts and decisions of the
Board, and any person may appeal any ruling or order of the Board to the Town
Council who may hear the matter and make the final decision.
(Ord. 07-2006, passed 4-18-2006) Penalty, see §
94.99
§ 94.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person who violates any section of this chapter shall be given
written notice of the violation by the Town Forester or his or her designee and
shall be instructed to remedy the violation within 30 days of notice.
   (B)   Any person who shall fail to remedy or abate the violation shall be
fined a sum not less than $50 and not to exceed $500 for each violation, plus
court costs.
   (C)   The town may commence an action to abate or enjoin the violations and/
or to assess the fines in any court with appropriate jurisdiction in the
county.
   (D)   In the event a lawsuit is commenced to abate the violations or to
assess a fine against a person and the person is found to have failed to remedy
a violation, the person shall be responsible and liable to the town for all
costs of that action, including but not limited to the costs and expenses of
remedying the violation, the costs of suit, expenses and reasonable attorney
fees incurred by the town in bringing the action.
(Ord. 07-2006, passed 4-18-2006)
CHAPTER 95: FAIR HOUSING
Section
   
95.01   Policy statement
   
95.02   Definitions
   
95.03   Unlawful practice
   
95.04   Sale or rental of housing
   
95.05   Residential real estate
   
95.06   Provision of brokerage services
   
95.07   Interference, coercion or intimidation
   
95.08   Prevention of intimidation in fair housing cases
   
95.09   Exemptions
   
95.10   Administrative enforcement
   
95.11   Separability; limitation of liability
§ 95.01 POLICY STATEMENT.
   It is the policy of the Town of Fremont, Indiana, to provide, within
constitutional limitation, for fair housing throughout its corporate limits as
provided for under the Federal Civil Rights Act of 1968, as amended, the
Federal Housing and Community Development Act of 1974, as amended, and I.C. 22-
9.5-1 et seq.
(1996 Code, § 7.5-1)
§ 95.02 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this chapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   AGGRIEVED PERSON. Includes any person who:
      (1)   Claims to have been injured by a discriminatory housing practice;
or
      (2)   Believes that a person will be injured by a discriminatory housing
practice that is about to occur.
   COMMISSION. The Indiana Civil Rights Commission created pursuant to I.C. 22-
9-1-4 et seq.
   COMPLAINANT. A person, including the Commission, who files a complaint under
I.C. 22-9.5-6.
   DISABILITY.
      (1)   With respect to a person:
         (a)   A physical or mental impairment which substantially limits 1 or
more of a person's major life activities;
         (b)   A record of having a like impairment;
         (c)   Being regarded as having a like impairment; and/or
         (d)   An impairment described or defined pursuant to the Federal
Americans with Disabilities Act of 1990, and any other impairment defined under
I.C. 22-9.5-2-2.
      (2)   The provisions of this definition notwithstanding, the term
DISABILITY does not include current illegal use of or addiction to a controlled
substance as defined in § 802 of Title 21 of the U.S.C.; nor does the term
DISABILITY include an individual solely because that individual is a
transvestite.
   DISCRIMINATORY HOUSING PRACTICE. An act that is unlawful under §§
95.04,
95.05,
95.06,
95.07,
95.08 or I.C. 22-9.5-5.
   DWELLING. Any building, structure or part of a building or structure that is
occupied as, or designed or intended for occupancy as, a residence by 1 or more
families; or any vacant land which is offered for sale or lease for the
construction or location of a building, structure or part of a building or
structure that is occupied as, or designed or intended for occupancy as a
residence by 1 or more families.
   FAMILIAL STATUS. Discrimination on the basis of FAMILIAL STATUS means
discrimination because the person is:
      (1)   Pregnant;
      (2)   Domiciled with an individual under the age of 18 years of age in
regard to whom the person is:
         (a)    The parent or legal custodian; or
         (b)   Has the written permission of the parent or legal custodian for
domicile with that person; or
      (3)   In the process of obtaining legal custody of an individual younger
than 18 years of age.
   FAMILY. An individual (I.C. § 22-9.5-2-9) or individuals having familial
status as that term is defined in this section.
   PERSON. Includes 1 or more individuals, corporations, partnerships,
associations, labor organizations, legal representatives, mutual companies,
joint-stock companies, trusts, non-incorporated organizations, trustees,
trustees in cases under Title 11 of the U.S.C., receivers and fiduciaries.
   TO RENT. Includes to lease, to sublease, to let and otherwise to grant for a
consideration the right to occupy the premises not owned by the occupant.
(I.C. 22-9.5-2-13)
(1996 Code, § 7.5-2)
§ 95.03 UNLAWFUL PRACTICE.
   Subject to the provisions of division (B) below, §
95.09 below and I.C. 22-9.5-3, the prohibitions against discrimination in the
sale or rental of housing set forth in I.C. 22-9.5-5-1 and in §
95.04 below apply to:
   (A)   All dwellings except as exempted by division (B) below and I.C. 22-
9.5-3.
   (B)   Other than the provisions of division (C) below, nothing in §
95.04 is to apply to:
      (1)   Any single-family house sold or rented by owner where the private
individual owner does not own more than 3 single-family houses at any 1 time;
provided that in the sale of a single-family house by a private individual
owner not residing in the house at the time of sale or who was not the most
recent resident of the house prior to the sale, the exemption only applies to 1
sale within any 24-month period. The private individual owner may not own any
interest in, nor have owned or reserved on his or her behalf, title to or any
right to all or a portion of the proceeds from the sale or rental of more than
3 single-family houses at any 1 time. The sale or rental of any single-family
house is sold or rented:
         (a)   Without the use in any manner of the sales or rental facilities
or services of any real estate broker, agent or salesperson, or any person in
the business of selling or renting dwellings, or any employee or agent of any
broker, agent or salesperson;
         (b)   Without the publication, posting or mailing, after notice of
advertisement or written notice in violation of §
95.04(C), but nothing in this provision shall prohibit the use of attorneys,
escrow agents, abstracters, title companies and other professional assistance
as necessary to perfect or transfer title.
      (2)   Rooms or units in dwellings containing living quarters occupied or
intended to be occupied by no more than 4 families living independently of each
other, if the owner actually maintains and occupies 1 of the living quarters as
his or her residence.
   (C)   For the purposes of division (B) above, a person shall be deemed to be
in the business of selling or renting dwellings if:
      (1)   He or she has, within the preceding 12 months, participated as
principal in 3 or more transactions involving the sale or rental of any
dwelling or any interest therein;
      (2)   He or she has, within the preceding 12 months, participated as
agent, other than in the sale of his or her own personal residence, in
providing sales or rental facilities or services in 2 or more transactions
involving the sale or rental of any dwelling or any interest therein; or
      (3)   He or she is the owner of any dwelling unit designed or intended
for occupancy by, or occupied by, 5 or more families.
(1996 Code, § 7.5-3)
§ 95.04 SALE OR RENTAL OF HOUSING.
   As made applicable by §
95.03 above and except as exempted by §§
95.03(B) and
95.09, it shall be unlawful:
   (A)   To refuse to sell or rent after the making of a bona fide offer, or to
refuse to negotiate for the sale or rental of, or otherwise make unavailable or
deny, a dwelling to any person because of race, color, religion, sex, familial
status or national origin;
   (B)   To discriminate against any person in the terms, conditions or
privileges of sale or rental of a dwelling, or in the provision of services or
facilities in connection therewith, because of race, color, religion, sex,
familial status or national origin;
   (C)   To make, print or publish, or cause to be made, printed or published
any notice, statement or advertisement, with respect to the sale or rental of a
dwelling that indicates any preference, limitation or discrimination based on
race, color, religion, sex, disability, familial status or national origin or
an intention to make any like preference, limitation or discrimination;
   (D)   To represent to any person because of race, color, religion, sex,
disability, familial status or national origin that any dwelling is not
available for inspection, sale or rental when the dwelling is in fact so
available;
   (E)   For profit, to induce or attempt to induce any person to sell or rent
any dwelling by representations regarding the entry or perspective entry into
the neighborhood of a person or persons of a particular race, color, religion,
sex, disability, familial status or national origin; and
   (F)   (1)   To discriminate in the sale or rental, or to otherwise make
unavailable or deny, a dwelling to any buyer or renter because of a disability
of:
         (a)   That person;
         (b)   A person residing in or intending to reside in that dwelling
after it is sold, rented or made available; or
         (c)   Any person associated with that person.
      (2)   For purposes of this division, DISCRIMINATION includes:
         (a)   A refusal to permit, at the expense of the disabled person,
reasonable modifications of existing premises occupied or to be occupied by
that person if modifications may be necessary to afford the person full
enjoyment of the premises except that, in the case of a rental, the landlord
may where it is reasonable to do so condition permission for a modification on
the renter agreeing to restore the interior of the premises to the condition
that existed before the modification, reasonable wear and tear excepted; or
         (b)   A refusal to make reasonable accommodations in rules, policies,
practices or services, when accommodations may be necessary to afford a person
equal opportunity to use and enjoy a dwelling.
      (3)   Nothing in this division requires a dwelling to be made available
to an individual whose tenancy would constitute a direct threat to the health
or safety of other individuals of whose tenancy would result in substantial
physical damage to the property of others.
      (4)   Nothing in this division requires, with respect to a rental
property or property sold on an installment basis, a landlord or contract
seller to allow modifications to a dwelling which will irreparably destroy the
original design of a home which was built over 50 years previously or which was
custom built for the owner as a residence; nor shall it require a landlord or
contract seller to allow modifications which would substantially reduce the
value of the property where the landlord or contract seller has reasonable
doubt as to the financial capability of the renter or buyer to restore the
dwelling to its original state upon termination of the lease or default upon
the contract by the buyer.
(1996 Code, § 7.5-4)
§ 95.05 RESIDENTIAL REAL ESTATE.
   (A)   It shall be unlawful for any person or other entity whose business
includes engaging in residential real estate-related transactions to
discriminate against any person in making available a transaction, or in the
terms or conditions of a transaction, because of race, color, religion, sex,
disability, familial status or national origin.
   (B)   As used in this section, the term RESIDENTIAL REAL ESTATE-RELATED
TRANSACTION means any of the following:
      (1)   The making or purchasing of loans or providing other financial
assistance:
         (a)   For purchasing, constructing, improving, repairing or
maintaining a dwelling; or
         (b)   Secured by residential real estate.
      (2)   The selling, brokering or appraising of residential real property.
   (C)   Nothing in this chapter prohibits a person engaged in the business of
furnishing appraisals of real property to take into consideration factors other
than race, color, religion, national origin, sex, disability or familial
status.
(1996 Code, § 7.5-5)
§ 95.06 PROVISION OF BROKERAGE SERVICES.
   It is unlawful to deny any person access to or membership or participation
in any multiple-listing service, real estate brokers' organization or other
service, organization or facility relating to the business of selling or
renting dwellings, or to discriminate against him or her in the terms or
conditions of access, membership or participation, on account of race, color,
religion, sex, disability, familial status or national origin.
(1996 Code, § 7.5-6)
§ 95.07 INTERFERENCE, COERCION OR INTIMIDATION.
   It is unlawful to coerce, intimidate, threaten or interfere with any person
in the exercise or enjoyment of, or on account of his or her having exercised
or enjoyed, or on account of his or her having aided or encouraged any other
person in the exercise of any right granted or protected by §§
95.03,
95.04,
95.05 or
95.06.
(1996 Code, § 7.5-7)
§ 95.08 PREVENTION OF INTIMIDATION IN FAIR HOUSING CASES.
   Whoever, whether or not acting under color of law, by force or threat of
force willfully injuries, intimidates or interferes with, or attempts to
injure, intimidate or interfere with:
   (A)   Any person because of his or her race, color, religion, sex,
disability, familial status or national origin and because he or she is or has
been selling, purchasing, renting, financing, occupying or contracting or
negotiating for the sale, purchase, rental, financing or occupation of any
dwelling, or applying for or participating in any service, organization or
facility relating to the business of selling or renting dwellings;
   (B)   Any person because he or she is or has been, or in order to intimidate
a person or any other person or any class of persons from:
      (1)   Participating, without discrimination on account of race, color,
religion, sex, disability, familial status or national origin, in any of the
activities, services, organizations or facilities; or
      (2)   Affording another person or class of persons opportunity or
protection so to participate.
   (C)   Any citizen because he is or has been lawfully aiding or encouraging
other persons to participate, without discrimination on account of race, color,
religion, sex, disability, familial status or national origin, in any of the
activities, services, organizations or facilities described in division (A)
above, or is or has participated lawfully in speech or peaceful assembly
opposing any denial of the opportunity to participate; or
   (D)   Any person violating the provisions of this section shall be guilty of
a violation and the town, or any party aggrieved by the violation shall be
entitled to seek and received injunctive relief to require cessation of any
violations, or future violations.
(1996 Code, § 7.5-8)
§ 95.09 EXEMPTIONS.
   (A)   Exemptions defined or set forth under I.C. 22-9.5-3 et seq. shall be
exempt from the provisions of this chapter to include those activities or
organizations set forth under divisions (B) and (C) below.
   (B)   Nothing in this chapter is to prohibit a religious organization,
association or society, or any non-profit institution or organization operated,
supervised or controlled by or in conjunction with a religious organization,
association or society, from limiting the sale, rental or occupancy of
dwellings which it owns or operates for other than a commercial purpose to
persons of the same religion, or from giving preference to those persons,
unless membership in a religion is restricted on account of race, color or
national origin. Nor does anything in the chapter prohibit a private club not
in fact open to the public, which as an incident to its primary purposes
provides lodgings which it owns or operates for other than a commercial
purpose, from limiting the rental and occupancy of lodgings to its members or
from giving preference to its members.
   (C)   (1)   Nothing in this chapter regarding familial status shall apply
with respect to housing for older persons.
      (2)   As used in this section, HOUSING FOR OLDER PERSONS means housing:
         (a)   Provided under any state or federal program that the Secretary
of the Federal Department of Housing and Urban Development or the State Civil
Rights Commission determines is specifically designed and operated to assist
elderly persons (as defined in the state or federal program);
         (b)   Intended for, and solely occupied by, persons 62 years of age or
older; or
         (c)   Intended and operated for occupancy by at least 1 person 55
years of age or older per unit.
(1996 Code, § 7.5-9)
§ 95.10 ADMINISTRATIVE ENFORCEMENT.
   (A)   The authority and responsibility for administering this chapter is
vested in the Indiana Civil Rights Commission for administrative enforcement of
actions pursuant to I.C. 22-9.5-6 and the Clerk-Treasurer of the town is the
designated person to receive any complaints brought to the attention of the
town and is responsible for forwarding all formal complaints of violations of
the provisions of this chapter to the Commission.
   (B)   All departments, officers and agencies of the Town of Fremont, Indiana
shall carry out their administrative duties pertaining to the departments,
programs and activities relating to housing and urban development in a manner
consistent with the purposes of this chapter and are to cooperate with the
officers involved with the administration thereof and the Commission to further
those purposes.
   (C)   The Clerk-Treasurer of the town of Fremont, Indiana, shall provide
information available to any aggrieved person or complainant requesting
information as may be provided to the town from time to time, along with a copy
of the provisions of this chapter if so requested, along with the address of
the Commission.
(1996 Code, § 7.5-10)
§ 95.11 SEPARABILITY; LIMITATION OF LIABILITY.
   (A)   If any provision of this chapter or the application thereof to any
person or circumstances shall be determined to be invalid, the remainder of the
chapter and the application of its provisions to other persons not similarly
situated or to other circumstances shall not be affected thereby.
(1996 Code, § 7.5-11)
   (B)   Nothing in this chapter is to be construed as imposing upon the town
or any town officer administering the same any liability in addition to any the
town or the official would have otherwise been subjected to had this chapter
not been adopted. Whenever any violation of this chapter is also a violation of
state or federal law, and a state or federal agency, officer, commission or
board has jurisdiction to prosecute under the state or federal law, then the
town shall defer to the state or federal agency, officer, commission or board
in the enforcement thereof. In addition, whenever any aggrieved party has
available to the party relief in the form of civil penalties or injunctive
rights as against a violator of this chapter, then the town shall defer to the
party in the initiation of any enforcement of this chapter. Provided, however,
when the town has been provided a written opinion by legal counsel stating that
the state, federal law, or the availability of civil penalties or injunctive
rights are not as extensive as are provided by the terms of this chapter, or
are inadequate to cause cessation of violations of the chapter, then the Town
Council may approve the initiation of enforcement of the chapter directly.
(1996 Code, § 7.5-12)
CHAPTER 96: FIREWORKS
Section
   
96.01   Definitions
   
96.02   Consumer fireworks
   
96.03   Permitted times
   
96.04   Exceptions
   
96.05   Prohibition in times of drought
 
   
96.99   Penalty
Cross-reference:
   Burning and fire regulations, see §§
91.015 through
91.022
§ 96.01 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this chapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   CONSUMER FIREWORKS. A small firework that is designed primarily to produce
visible or audible effects by combustion, and that is required to comply with
the construction, chemical composition, and labeling regulations promulgated by
the United States Consumer Product Safety Commission under 16 C.F.R. 1507. The
term also include some small devices designed to produce and audible effect,
such as whistling devices, ground devices containing 50 milligrams or less of
explosive composition, and aerial devices containing 130 milligrams or less of
explosive composition. Propelling or expelling charges consisting of a mixture
of charcoal, sulfur, and potassium nitrate are not considered as designed to
produce an audible effect.
(Ord. 2007-10, passed 8-21-2007; Am. Ord. 2014-06, passed 11-18-2014; Am. Ord.
2016-07, passed 9-20-2016)
§ 96.02 CONSUMER FIREWORKS.
   (A)    Consumer fireworks include:
      (1)   Aerial devices, which include sky rockets, missile type rockets,
helicopter or aerial spinners, roman candles, mines, and shells;
      (2)   Ground audible devices, which include firecrackers, salutes, and
chasers; and
      (3)   Firework devices containing combinations of the effects described
in division (A)(1) and (2) of this section.
   (B)    Consumer fireworks shall not include the following items referenced
in I.C. 22-11-14-8(a):
      (1)   Dipped sticks or wire sparklers. However, the total pyrotechnic
composition may not exceed 100 grams per item. Device containing chlorate or
perchlorate salts may not exceed 5 grams in total composition per item;
      (2)   Cylindrical fountains;
      (3)   Cone fountains;
      (4)   Illuminating torches;
      (5)   Wheels;
      (6)   Ground spinners;
      (7)   Filter sparklers;
      (8)   Snakes or glow worms;
      (9)   Smoke devices; and
      (10)   Trick noisemakers, which include:
         (a)   Party poppers;
         (b)   Booby traps;
         (c)   Snappers;
         (d)   Trick matches;
         (e)   Cigarette loads; and
         (f)   Auto burglar alarms.
(Ord. 2007-10, passed 8-21-2007; Am. Ord. 2014-06, passed 11-18-2014; Am. Ord.
2016-07, passed 9-20-2016)
§ 96.03 PERMITTED TIMES.
   No person within the Town of Fremont, Indiana, shall use, ignite, or
discharge or permit to be used, ignited, or discharged any type of consumer
fireworks on any day at any time other than the following:
   (A)   Between the hours of 5:00 p.m. and 2 hours after sunset on June 29,
June 30, July 1, July 2, July 3, July 5, July 6, July 7, July 8, and July 9;
   (B)   Between the hours of 10:00 a.m. and 12:00 midnight on July 4;
   (C)   Between the hours of 10:00 a.m. on December 31 and 1:00 a.m. on
January 1; and
   (D)   Between the hours of 10:00 a.m. and 2 hours after sunset on the
Saturday during the Fremont Music Fest, except as this subpart may from time to
time conflict with an allowable date and time provided for under division (A)
of this section.
(Ord. 2007-10, passed 8-21-2007; Am. Ord. 2014-06, passed 11-18-2014; Am. Ord.
2016-07, passed 9-20-2016)
§ 96.04 EXCEPTIONS.
   Notwithstanding any provision to the contrary, Fremont High School is
permitted to use fireworks at home football games.
(Ord. 2016-07, passed 9-20-2016)
§ 96.05 PROHIBITION IN TIMES OF DROUGHT.
   Notwithstanding any provisions to the contrary, when it is necessary for the
protection of public health and safety, such as in conditions of extreme
drought, the Town Council of the Town of Fremont may prohibit the use of any
and all consumer fireworks. The Town Council may only prohibit the use of any
and all consumer fireworks for so long as the emergency or conditions justify
their prohibition.
(Ord. 2007-10, passed 8-21-2007; Am. Ord. 2014-06, passed 11-18-2014; Am. Ord.
2016-07, passed 9-20-2016)
§ 96.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   The Fremont Police Department shall be charged with enforcing the
provisions of this chapter.
   (B)   Any person, firm, corporation, or association violating the provisions
of this chapter commits a Class C infraction and shall be fined in the amount
of $100 for each violation. Violations of this chapter shall be prosecuted
through the Steuben County Courts.
(Ord. 2007-10, passed 8-21-2007; Am. Ord. 2014-06, passed 11-18-2014; Am. Ord.
2016-07, passed 9-20-2016)

§ 110.01 AUTHORITY TO LICENSE.
   The town has the authority to impose a license fee that is reasonably
related to the administrative cost of exercising the regulating powers.
(1996 Code, § 4-1)
§ 110.02 APPLICATION AND FEE.
   All applications for a permit or license under this chapter shall be
referred by the Clerk-Treasurer to the Town Council.
(1996 Code, § 4-2)
§ 110.03 APPROVAL OF TOWN COUNCIL.
   After examination, the Town Council may grant a permit or license at the
next regular meeting, unless good cause be shown why a permit or license should
not be granted.
(1996 Code, § 4-3)
§ 110.04 DURATION OF LICENSE; DISPLAY REQUIRED; INSPECTIONS.
   (A)   All licenses issued under this chapter, unless specified otherwise on
the license, shall be issued for the duration of the calendar year for which
they were issued, and shall expire on December 31.
   (B)   Every person who is issued a license under the provisions of the
licensed activity is being conducted, or if there are no premises shall carry
the license while engaged in the activity for which he or she has been
licensed, and shall exhibit it to any town official or citizen upon request.
   (C)   The Town Marshal or his or her designee may inspect all places of
business under license or required to have a license.
(1996 Code, § 4-4)
§ 110.05 ISSUANCE; REVOCATION OF SUSPENSION.
   (A)    The Clerk-Treasurer shall issue licenses upon payment of the license
fees and compliance with the applicable provisions of this code, and Town
Council approval.
   (B)   Licenses issued by the town may be revoked or suspended if the person
holding the license has violated the terms or conditions of the license or the
law under which it was issued, or had conducted the business in a manner so as
to constitute a threat to public health, safety or general welfare of the
town’s citizens.
(1996 Code, § 4-5)

GENERALLY
§ 111.01 POLICIES FOR CIVIC, EDUCATION, COMMUNITY EVENTS.
   (A)   The town will offer reasonable assistance and temporarily close off
streets without Town Council approval for funeral processions, to allow for
orderly ingress and egress to and from civic, educational and other similar
crowd gathering events, for parades pertaining to local school district events,
and for fire trucks and other emergency vehicles.
   (B)   The town will offer reasonable assistance and temporarily close off
streets with Town Council approval for community-sponsored street fairs,
festivals and centennials where the primary purpose is to raise funds for non-
profit community-centered projects of a charitable nature, educational events
sponsored by the local associations or commercial promotions in the downtown
areas at the request of a substantial majority of the downtown merchants.
   (C)   The town, upon Council approval, will offer reasonable assistance and
temporarily close streets for other community events which do not involve the
town in essentially private matters and are not likely to cause or result in
actions injurious to the public health, safety and welfare. No action shall be
taken upon requests until the Council has been apprised of the impacts of the
request on state highways.
(1996 Code, § 4-9)
§ 111.02 STREET PERFORMANCES, SHOWS AND EXHIBITIONS.
   (A)   Any person or persons who shall exhibit or participate in exhibiting
for any purpose of gain either to himself or herself or others or for any
purpose whatever within the Town of Fremont, Indiana, any theatrical
performance, show or puppets, exhibition of tumbling or performing, wire or
rope walking, dancing, sleight of hand performances of any kind, or show of any
kind or nature, without first having obtained or procured from the Town of
Fremont, Indiana, a license to do so, shall upon conviction be fined in the sum
of $25.
   (B)   Each and every performance or exhibition shall constitute a separate
offense.
   (C)   Any person or persons who desiring to obtain a license as hereinbefore
specified shall pay to the Clerk-Treasurer of the Town of Fremont, Indiana, the
sum of $4 for each and every day the performance or exhibition shall be held.
(1996 Code, § 4-10) Penalty, see §
111.99
§ 111.03 BILLIARD TABLES AND THE LIKE.
   (A)   Any person desiring to obtain a license to operate billiard tables,
pool tables, bowling alleys or any kind of gaming tables in the Town of
Fremont, County of Steuben, State of Indiana, shall pay to the Clerk-Treasurer
of the town the sum of $10 for each billiard table, pool table, bowling alley
or any kind of gaming table he or she may wish to operate and shall be issued
to the applicant a license to operate tables or alleys in the town for a term
of 1 year which license shall be signed by the Clerk-Treasurer and President of
the Town Council.
   (B)   If any person in the Town of Fremont, Steuben County, State of
Indiana, owning or having the care, management or control of any billiard
table, pool table, bowling alley or any kind of gaming table and operating the
same for gain shall permit any person to play billiards, pool or any other game
at or upon a table or tables or alley without first procuring from the Town
Council a license to do so heretofore provided, shall be deemed guilty of a
violation and shall on conviction thereof be fined $10 for each offense.
(1996 Code, § 4-12)
§ 111.04 GARAGE SALES, PORCH SALES AND THE LIKE.
   (A)   It shall be unlawful for any person, residence, firm or corporation to
hold or conduct a garage sale, yard sale, porch sale or similar events within
the Town of Fremont, unless a permit therefore shall first have been obtained
from the Clerk-Treasurer of Fremont.
   (B)   The Clerk-Treasurer shall issue a permit upon payment of $2; provided,
however, no charge shall be made if the applicant is a charitable, religious,
educational organization or merchant sidewalk sale.
   (C)   Any permit so issued shall be valid for the time specified in the
permit but in no event for more than 3 successive days.
   (D)   No permit shall be issued to any person, residence, firm or
corporation who shall have been issued 2 permits within the preceding 12
months.
   (E)   Any person, residence, firm or corporation who shall hold or conduct
any sale or event without having first obtained a permit shall upon conviction
be fined in any amount no exceeding $300.
   (F)   Garage sale, porch sale or yard sale includes all general sales, open
to the public, advertised or unadvertised, conducted from or on property within
the Town of Fremont, as defined by the zoning ordinance, for the purpose of
disposing of property including, but not limited to, all sales entitled
“garage,” “lawn,” “yard,” “attic,” “porch,” “room,” “backyard,” “patio,” “flea
market” or “rummage” sale.
(1996 Code, § 4-13)
§ 111.05 LIQUOR RETAILER'S PERMIT.
   The consent of the town is given and granted to the proper legal authorities
of the State of Indiana, to issue liquor retailer’s permits for the sale of
alcoholic, spirituous beverages to applicants otherwise duly qualified to
premises within the town consistent with all applicable state law.
(1996 Code, § 4-14)
§ 111.06 PARK PAVILION RENTALS, GARAGE SALES AND FARMERS MARKET VENDOR PERMIT
FEES.
   (A)   Park pavilion rentals. The town park pavilion rental permit fee shall
be increased from $25 to $30.
   (B)   Garage sale, yard sale and the like. The garage sale permit fee shall
be increased from $2 to $5 per permit.
   (C)   Farmers market vendor permit. The farmers market vendor permit fee
shall be increased from $20 per year to $25.
(Ord. 2010-05, passed 2-16-2010)
AUCTIONEERS, PEDDLERS AND ITINERANT MERCHANTS
§ 111.15 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this subchapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   PEDDLER.
      (1)   Any person traveling by foot, wagon, automotive vehicle or any
other type of conveyance from place to place, from house to house or from
street to street carrying, conveying or transporting goods, wares, merchandise,
food products, offering and exposing them for sale or making sales and
delivering articles to purchasers, or who, without traveling from place to
place, shall sell or offer the same for sale from a wagon, automotive vehicle,
railroad car or other vehicle or conveyance.
      (2)   However, one who solicits orders and as a separate transaction
makes deliveries to purchasers as a part of a scheme or design to evade the
provisions of this subchapter shall be deemed a PEDDLER subject to the
provisions of this chapter.
      (3)   This definition, however, shall not be construed to include
commercial travelers or salespersons calling exclusively upon businesses,
professional persons, schools or public institutions for the purpose of taking
orders or selling books, equipment, supplies or services used professionally
thereby, and shall not be construed to include persons selling exclusively
products grown by these persons. The word PEDDLER shall include the words
HAWKER or HUCKSTER.
   SOLICITOR. 
      (1)   Any person traveling from place to place, from house to house or
from street to street within the town, or contacting persons by telephone
within the town, for the purpose of taking orders for the sale of goods, wares,
merchandise, magazines, books or personal property of any nature whatsoever for
a future delivery, or for services to be furnished or performed in the future
regardless of whether the person has, carries or exposes for sale a sample of
the subject of the sale or whether he or she is collecting advance payments on
the sales or who solicits monies door-to-door for non-profit or not-for-profit
organizations.
      (2)   This definition, however, shall not include commercial travelers or
salespersons calling exclusively upon businesses, professional persons, schools
or public institutions for the purpose of taking orders or selling books,
equipment, supplies or services used professionally thereby. The word SOLICITOR
shall include the word CANVASSER.
   TRANSIENT MERCHANT.
      (1)   Any person, whether as owner, agent, consignee or employee, who
engages in a temporary business of selling and delivering goods, wares and
merchandise within the town, and who, in furtherance of this purpose, hires,
leases, uses or occupies any building, structure, motor vehicle, tent, railroad
boxcar, boat, public room in hotels, motels, lodging houses, apartments, shops,
or any street, alley or other place within the town, for the exhibition and
sale of the goods, wares and merchandise, either privately or at public
auction.
      (2)   However, this definition shall not be construed to include any
person who, while occupying temporary location, does not sell from stock, but
exhibits samples only for the purpose of securing orders for future delivery
only, and this definition shall not be construed to include any person who is a
commercial traveler or salesperson calling exclusively upon businesses,
professional persons, schools or public institutions for the purpose of taking
orders or selling books, equipment, supplies or services used professionally
thereby, and further shall not be construed to include any person selling
exclusively products grown by that person.
      (3)   A person shall be a TRANSIENT MERCHANT even though he or she
temporarily associates with a local dealer, trader, merchant or auctioneer, or
conducts the transient business in connection with, as a part of, or in the
name of any local dealer, trader, merchant or auctioneer. The term TRANSIENT
MERCHANT shall include the terms ITINERANT MERCHANT and ITINERANT VENDOR.
(Ord. 2000-4, passed 4-10-2000)
§ 111.16 LICENSE REQUIRED.
   (A)   It shall be unlawful for a transient merchant, peddler or solicitor to
engage in their respective businesses within the town without obtaining a
license in compliance with the provisions of this chapter. The obtaining of a
license by an employer or principal shall in no way relieve any employee or
agent of that employer or principal of his or her legal obligation to obtain a
license, if his or her activity falls within the definition set out in §
111.15.
   (B)   Licenses issued under the provisions of this subchapter shall contain
the information and be in the form prescribed by the Town Council.
   (C)   It shall be unlawful for a transient merchant, peddler or solicitor to
engage in his or her respective business within the town at any time between
the hours of 8:00 a.m. and 5:00 p.m. The license to be issued shall show on its
face that there shall be no door-to-door solicitations after sundown or before
sunup.
(Ord. 2000-4, passed 4-10-2000)
§ 111.17 APPLICATION.
   (A)   All applicants for a license under this chapter shall file a written
sworn application signed by the applicant or his or her agent.
   (B)   In addition to any information the Clerk-Treasurer may deem necessary
for the effective implementation of this chapter, the application shall
contain, and the applicant shall provide the following:
      (1)   The name and permanent address of the applicant;
      (2)   The local address or addresses of the applicant;
      (3)   If the applicant is a partnership, the names of the partners; and
if the applicant is a corporation, the name of the president of the corporation
and the state of incorporation;
      (4)   A statement as to whether the business will be conducted from fixed
locations, and if so, the addresses of those locations;
      (5)   The length of time for which the applicant is requesting the
license. (Any part of a day shall be considered a full day and licenses shall
be issued only for consecutive days);
      (6)   Fingerprints of the persons authorized by the applicant to transact
business under the license;
      (7)   A statement of the nature and character of the goods, wares or
merchandise to be sold;
      (8)   A listing of communities the applicant has conducted transient
business in within the last 6 months prior to the date of application;
      (9)   The state identification number of the business, if required; and
      (10)   A statement of whether the business holds a current Indiana retail
merchant’s certificate, and if so, the name, mailing address and main location
of the business the license is issued to, and the date of expiration if a
license is required.
(Ord. 2000-4, passed 4-10-2000)
§ 111.18 BOND.
   (A)   (1)   At the time of filing the application and as a part thereof, the
applicant shall file and deposit with the Clerk-Treasurer, a bond in the penal
sum of $1,000 in cash, or a bond payable to the Town of Fremont secured by a
surety having his or her principal place of business in Indiana.
      (2)   The bond and surety must be approved by the Clerk-Treasurer. The
bond must be valid for 365 days.
      (3)   The bond must be payable to the Town of Fremont who is named as
agent for service of process by both you and the surety.
      (4)   The bond proceeds are first to be for the use and benefit of the
town to pay for any fines, court costs and judgments that may be assessed
against the applicant, its agents or employees, in favor of the town for the
violation of any provisions of this town code.
      (5)   The remainder of the bond shall be for the use and benefit of any
purchasers of any goods, wares or merchandise who might have a cause of action
against the applicant rising from or out of the sale or sales.
   (B)   Unless the Clerk-Treasurer is given written notification of a pending
cause of action by the town or any person within 1 year from the date of
expiration of the license, the Clerk-Treasurer shall release the bond 1 year
after the expiration of the license.
(Ord. 2000-4, passed 4-10-2000)
§ 111.19 ISSUANCE OF LICENSE.
   (A)   (1)   Upon the filing of the application and after the applicant has
established that he or she has fully complied with all provisions of this
chapter, the Clerk-Treasurer may issue to the applicant a license authorizing
the applicant to transact business as proposed in the application.
      (2)   The license shall not be transferable and shall be valid only in
the Town of Fremont.
      (3)   If the Clerk-Treasurer determines prior to issuing a license that
any fraud, misrepresentation or false statement are contained in the
application for the license, no license shall be issued.
   (B)   If an applicant proposes to transact business from more than 1
location, the applicant shall obtain a separate license, and pay the fee
therefore, for each location before transacting any business.
   (C)   (1)   If an applicant proposes to transact business in this town from
other than a fixed location, the applicant shall apply for and the Clerk-
Treasurer may grant a mobile transient merchant license.
      (2)   A separate license shall be obtained for each employee, agent or
other person transacting business for and on behalf of the applicant.
(Ord. 2000-4, passed 4-10-2000)
§ 111.20 LICENSE FEES.
   (A)   There shall be a base annual fee for each transient merchant's license
and each mobile transient merchant's license in the amount of $200 which shall
be valid for 365 days from the date of issuance.
   (B)   In addition, the fee for a transient merchant's license shall be $10
per day for each location and for a mobile transient merchant's license shall
be $10 per day for each employee, agent or other person transacting business
for and on behalf of the applicant in the town.
   (C)   The license can be renewed for as many days as the applicant chooses
by prepayment of the sum of $10 per day.
(Ord. 2000-4, passed 4-10-2000)
§ 111.21 BADGE AND VEHICLE SIGN; DISPLAY.
   (A)   (1)   When any license is issued pursuant to this subchapter, the
person to whom the license is issued shall be supplied by the Clerk-Treasurer,
without additional charge, with a badge stamped or marked “Licensed Peddler”
and it shall be numbered.
      (2)   The dates which the license is valid for shall be so indicated on
the badge.
      (3)   The peddler shall keep the badge plainly displayed on the outside
of his or her coat or clothes when engaged in peddling and shall surrender it
on the expiration of the license.
   (B)   (1)   Every person licensed to hawk or peddle with a vehicle or
handcart shall be supplied by the Clerk-Treasurer, without additional charge,
with a substantial magnetic sign bearing the name “Licensed Peddler” in letters
not less than 3-1/2 inches in height and numbered.
      (2)   This sign shall be conspicuously attached and fastened to the
vehicle so as to be plainly visible by all persons doing business with the
peddler.
      (3)   The magnetic sign shall remain the property of the town and be
returned by the peddler when the license expires.
(Ord. 2000-4, passed 4-10-2000)
§ 111.22 APPROVAL.
   (A)   Upon compliance by the applicant with the provisions of §
111.17, the Town Marshal shall stamp his or her approval on the application
blank submitted by the applicant.
   (B)   The Town Marshal shall not be required to grant approval to any person
who has been convicted of any felony or misdemeanor involving moral turpitude
or any violation of this chapter.
(Ord. 2000-4, passed 4-10-2000)
§ 111.23 STAMPED CREDENTIALS NONTRANSFERABLE.
   Stamped credentials shall be nontransferable and shall entitle the holder
thereof, for the period indicated therein, unless revoked, to solicit orders
within the town for the purchase of the merchandise specified in his or her
application; however, the holder shall have his or her stamped credentials in
his or her possession at all times while soliciting orders and shall exhibit
them at any time upon request by any law enforcement officer of the town or any
purchaser or prospective purchaser.
(Ord. 2000-4, passed 4-10-2000)
§ 111.24 EXCEPTIONS AND EXEMPTIONS.
   (A)   (1)   This subchapter shall not apply to salespersons selling goods to
retail or wholesale stores for resale.
      (2)   Any person who has, and has had for the preceding 12 months, a
regular place of business within the town, and any person employed by or
soliciting for any person who has, and has had for the preceding 12 months, a
regular place of business within the town, shall not be required to register
before soliciting orders.
   (B)   The provisions of this chapter shall not apply to sales made to
dealers by commercial travelers or selling agents in the usual course of
business, or to sheriffs or other public officers selling goods, wares and
merchandise according to law, nor to bona-fide assignees or receivers appointed
in this state selling goods, wares and merchandise for the benefit of
creditors.
   (C)   In addition to any other exemptions allowed by this chapter, the
provisions of this chapter shall not apply to:
      (1)   Persons who sell goods, wares or merchandise for and on behalf of
any not-for-profit organization when the proceeds of sales inure to the benefit
of a not-for-profit organization, if the not-for-profit corporation is located
within Steuben County;
      (2)   Any person, individual, co-partner, limited liability company or
corporation which grows the goods, wares or merchandise that is sold or offered
for sale;
      (3)   A person who makes crafts or items by hand and sells them or offers
them for sale;
      (4)   An auctioneer who is licensed under I.C. 25-6.1;
      (5)   An organization that is exempt from the Indiana gross retail tax
under I.C. 6-2.5-5-26 (a charitable organization);
      (6)   A person who:
         (a)   Organizes;
         (b)   Sells merchandise;
         (c)   Offers to sell merchandise; or
         (d)   Exhibits at a trade show or convention.
      (7)   A person who holds a registered retail merchant's certificate under
I.C. 6-2.5-8.
(Ord. 2000-4, passed 4-10-2000)
§ 111.25 SELLING FOODSTUFFS; PHYSICAL EXAM.
   (A)   Any person, firm or corporation desiring to engage in the business of
solicitor or itinerant merchant who sells fruit, vegetables, bread, pastries or
other foodstuffs, which have not been canned shall, before receiving their
license or certificate as provided in §
111.19, present to the Clerk-Treasurer the certificate of a reputable doctor of
medicine to the approval of the Town Council certifying that the persons
handling the same are free from all venereal or transmittable diseases and
showing that the examination has been made within 30 days from the date of
receiving the license, and a new certificate shall be placed on file with the
Clerk-Treasurer within 30 days from the date of the first certificate so long
as the party shall continue to do business under the license.
   (B)   No person shall transact any business of selling foodstuffs in the
town under a solicitor's or itinerant merchant's license unless they shall have
a physical examination certificate which is dated not more than 30 days
therebefore.
(Ord. 2000-4, passed 4-10-2000)
§ 111.26 REVOCATION OF LICENSE.
   (A)   A license issued pursuant to this subchapter may be revoked by the
Clerk-Treasurer after notice and a hearing thereon, for any of the following
causes:
      (1)   Any fraud, misrepresentation or false statement contained in the
application for the license;
      (2)   Any fraud, misrepresentation or false statement made in connection
with the selling of goods, wares or merchandise;
      (3)   Any violation of this chapter;
      (4)   Conviction of the licensee of any felony or of a misdemeanor
involving moral turpitude; or
      (5)   Conducting the business licensed under this chapter in an unlawful
manner or in a manner so as to constitute a breach of the peace or to
constitute a menace to the health, safety or general welfare of the public.
   (B)   Notice of the revocation shall be given to the address or addresses as
provided in the application.
(Ord. 2000-4, passed 4-10-2000)
§ 111.27 RIGHT TO APPEAL.
   (A)   Any person aggrieved by the decision of the Clerk-Treasurer or the
Town Marshal in regard to the denial of a license as provided for in §
111.19 shall have the right to appeal to the Town Council.
   (B)   Appeal shall be taken by filing with the Council, within 14 days after
notice of the decision by the Clerk-Treasurer or the Town Marshal has been
mailed to the address provided in the application, a written statement setting
forth the grounds for the appeal.
   (C)   The Council shall set the time and place for a hearing on the appeal,
and notice of the hearing shall be given to the person in the same manner
unless the Town Council is provided with a different address to use.
   (D)   The order of the Council on the appeal shall be final.
(Ord. 2000-4, passed 4-10-2000)
§ 111.28 ENFORCING OFFICER.
   The Town Marshal or his or her deputy or any other person designated by the
Town Council, such as the Town Manager or Clerk-Treasurer or the Town Council
itself, is hereby authorized to enforce the provisions of this subchapter.
(Ord. 2000-4, passed 4-10-2000)
§ 111.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no
specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99.
   (B)   Any person, firm or corporation failing to comply with the provisions
of §§
111.15 et seq. shall be subject to a fine of $250 per day. A violation may be
enforced as set forth below by the Town Marshal issuing a citation. The
violation can be processed through the Town Court or the Clerk-Treasurer's
office at the discretion of the Town Council. Each day a violation continues
shall be deemed a separate violation during any 1 licensing period.
(Ord. 2000-4, passed 4-10-2000)
Editor’s note:
   There are 2 separate forms in this appendix. The first is an application
that is 5 pages long. The second is a certificate that is 1 page long.
